And the author of this book said when he completed for you, O people, this book which is a part of the science of medicine in its completeness and reached the goal in it from its clarity and explanation, I saw that I complete it for you with this article which is a part of work by hand.
Because work by hand is refined in our country and in our time entirely absent, to the point that its science was almost studied and its trace disappeared. And what remained from it are slight drawings in the books of the ancients which were corrected by hands and its errors and confusion were rectified until its meanings became obscured and its benefits disappeared.
So I saw that I revive it and compose in it this article on the path of explanation, clarification, and brevity and bring images of surgical instruments and all tools of work because it is from increasing clarity and aiding what needs it.
And the reason there is no skilled artisan by hand in our time because the craft of medicine is long and whoever wants to practice it must study before that the science of anatomy as described by Galen. Until he understands the benefits of the organs and their types and humors and connections and separations, and knows the bones, nerves, muscles, their number, exits, veins, arteries, and the places where they emerge.
Therefore, Albucasis said that physicians are many in name but few in deed, especially in the craft of the hand, and we mentioned a part of this in the introduction to this book.
Because whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned from anatomy, has inevitably fallen into errors that kill people, as I have seen often from those who imagined themselves in this science and claimed it without knowledge or study.
And that is because I saw a ignorant physician who incised a tumor of a pig's on a woman's neck, so he severed some of the arteries of the neck and blood gushed from the woman until she fell dead before his eyes.
And I saw another physician who advanced in removing a stone from a man whose tooth was inflamed, and the stone was large so it ruptured; he removed it with a piece from the bladder's wall. So the man died for about three days, and I was called to remove it; seeing the size of the stone and the condition of the sick person, I judged that outcome.
And I saw another physician who was making a living by treating some of our country's leaders.
So it happened to a young black boy who had a broken leg near the ankle with a wound; the physician, in his ignorance, quickly bound the fracture to the wound with splints and bandages tightly, not leaving any space for the wound to breathe.
Then he released him on his whims and left him for days, ordering him not to loosen the bandage until his leg and foot swelled; he was close to death.
So I was called to him and quickly loosened the bandage, he found relief and was free from his pain; except that the corruption had become firm in the limb and I could not reverse it.
And the corruption continued to spread in the member until it died.
And I saw another physician who treated a cancerous tumor and after days it increased until the patient's affliction became great, for if cancer is composed of black humors then it should not be treated with iron at all.
Except if it is in a member that can potentially be removed entirely.
And for this, my sons, it is necessary for you to learn that work with the hand is divided into two parts: work accompanied by safety and work that brings harm in most cases.
And I have warned in every place mentioned in this book the work that contains danger and fear, so it is necessary for you to avoid it and reject it.
Lest the ignorant find a way to slander and attack, take for yourselves firmness and caution, and rely on gentleness and steadfastness.
And use the best path leading to safety and a blessed outcome, and avoid dangerous and difficult illnesses that are hard to cure.
And be wary of what might cause you fear that doubt will enter into your religion and worldly affairs, for it is more beneficial for your worldly status and higher in this world and the hereafter for your fates.
For Galen said in some of his precepts, 'Do not treat a bad illness so that you are called bad physicians.'
And I have divided this article into three chapters.
The First Chapter.
On cauterization by fire and cauterization by a sharp drug, arranged from the century to antiquity and pictures of instruments and tools for cauterization and all that is needed in work with the hand.
And the Second Chapter.
On incision, poultice, phlebotomy, cupping, and surgeries, and extracting arrows and all of that kind, arranged,  and pictures of the instruments.
The third chapter.
Concerning fractures, dislocations, and treatment of the sciatic nerve, and similar ailments, it is arranged in order from the top to the bottom with pictures of the instruments.
The first chapter.
Concerning  the incision.
And before we mention how to perform it, it is necessary to mention its benefits and harms and in what temperament it is used.
And I say that the discussion of the benefits and harms of the incision is a long discourse and a precise science, and a hidden secret, and many of the wise men have spoken about it.
And they differed in it, and I have abbreviated from their sayings a little out of fear of prolixity.
And I say that the incision is beneficial in general for all bad temperaments that are with substance and without substance, except for two temperaments: which are the hot temperament without substance and the dry temperament without substance.
As for the dry temperament with substance, they differed in it, some saying that the incision is beneficial in it, and others saying the opposite, that the incision is not suitable in a disease that is from heat and dryness because the nature of fire is heat and dryness.
And it is impossible for a hot and dry disease to be cured by a hot and dry remedy, and the one who says the opposite says that the incision with fire can benefit from a hot and dry disease that occurs in people's bodies. Because when you add the body of man and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you make the body of man cold.
And I say what he says because experience has revealed it to me many times, except that it should not be imagined about this matter except by one who has practiced and trained in the science of incision extensively. And who stood on the differences of people's temperaments and the states of diseases within themselves, their causes, symptoms, and duration.
As for the rest of the humors, there is no fear from them, especially cold-wet diseases, which all physicians have agreed upon and have not differed in the benefit of purging them.
Know, O sons of physicians, that the secret of treatment is cauterization with fire and its superiority over cauterization with burning medicine because fire is a single essence whose action does not extend beyond the organ that is cauterized, nor does it harm another connected part except for slight harm.
And cauterization with burning medicine may exceed its action to what is beyond the organs and may cause disease in the organ that is difficult to treat, or even death, while fire, because of its honor and generosity of essence, does not do this except if it is excessive.
And this has become clear to us by experience through long service, attention to the craft, and standing upon the facts of the matter.
For this reason, I have dispensed with lengthy speech, although if it were fitting for this book of mine, I would have presented to you in fire a hidden secret and the manner of its action in bodies and its negation of diseases with philosophical and demonstrative discourse that penetrates your understanding.
Know, O sons of physicians, that they have differed in the time suitable for cauterization and have made the best time the spring season.
And I say that cauterization can be suitable in every time because the harm caused by time is overtaken by the benefit brought about by cauterization. Especially if the cauterization is from a necessary and strong pain that is pressing, not bearing delay because what may follow it is a calamity greater than the slight harm entering from time.
And do not conceive, O sons of physicians, what the common people and ignorant physicians imagine that cauterization which cures a disease does not return again ever and make it lasting.
They should not think, because of the kindling and drying effect of cautery that it is like a medicine which alters humors and dries up the superfluities which are the cause of pain.
But cautery surpasses medicine in the speed of its success, the strength of its action, and the intensity of its power.
And the disease may return after a while, depending on the patient's temperament, the strength of his illness and its establishment, and what is prepared in his body from the gathering of humors and his neglect in acquiring them from food and suchlike causes.
Except that the disease for which cautery is employed be a mild one and in a member with little humor and moisture. Like cauterizing a tooth for pain and the like, it may not return in that case, which is at the very least.
And as for the common saying that cautery is the last of remedies, it is a true saying not to what they go for because they believe no remedy will be effective after cautery by medicine or otherwise and the matter is otherwise.
And what is meant by cautery being the last of remedies is that when we have employed all kinds of treatments for a disease and those medicines have not been effective, then we employ the last thing which is cautery and it becomes effective from here it happens that cautery is the last of remedies. Not according to the meaning that the common people went for and many ignorant physicians.
And the ancients mentioned that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they said this because of the moderation of gold and the nobility of its essence, and they said it does not scald the place of cautery, which is not true at all.
Because I have tried it and found that it does that in some bodies but not others, and cautery with it is better and more preferable than iron as they said, except that if you heat the instrument of gold in the fire, it doesn't become clear to you when it heats to the degree you want for redness because of the gold.
For it hastens towards the cold and if you increase it with fever it melts in the fire and becomes dispersed, so that the maker falls into trouble from that. Therefore, iron became faster and closer to the right for us to work by God's will.
And I have arranged this chapter on cauterization into sections organized from the head to the foot, so that it is easier for the student what he wants from it by God's will.
The first section.
In cauterizing the head, there is one kind.
This cauterization is beneficial from the excess of moisture and coldness on the brain, which are the causes of headaches and an increase in discharges from the head towards the eyes and ears, as well as excessive sleep, toothache, and sore throat. And in general for every disease that appears from coldness like stroke, epilepsy, and muteness, and similar diseases.
The image of this cauterization is to order the sick person first to vomit with a laxative medicine that purifies the head for three nights or four, according to what the strength of the patient and his disposition and habit require.
Then order him to shave his head with a razor, then sit him down in front of you, seated with his hands on his chest.
Then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his eyes, and where your middle finger ends, mark that place with charcoal.
Then heat the cautery iron, which its image is....
When a part of the bone becomes exposed like the size of a hazelnut or a grain of wheat, raise your hand, otherwise, return your hand with the same iron or another if it cooled. Until you see from the bone what I told you, then take something of salt, dissolve it in water, and soak a cotton swab in it, place it on the site, and leave it for three days.
Then place upon it cotton soaked in tallow and leave it on until the char has gone from the fire, then treat it with the quaternary ointment until it heals, God willing.
And they have said that the wound, every time it remains open, produces pus which is better and more beneficial.
And some of them have mentioned that the skin should be cauterized to the bone, and hold the cautery until some thickness of bone burns, then after that strip what has burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others have said that it is necessary to exaggerate the cauterizing until it affects the bone strongly, so that it falls from the bone like a diamond or a small meteorite, and they claimed that it releases steam from the head from that place and leave the wound open for a long time.
Then treat it until it closes, and I do not see these two types of cauterization at all except in some people and on the path of deception, and leaving it with me is better, and with safety if it exists, because the head increases when its natural connection is broken, as we have seen in other limbs.
Especially when the patient's head is naturally weak, and the first type of cauterization is safer and better with me, and by it I work, do so safely God willing.
The second chapter.
In the skull as well.
If a chronic headache occurs in the general head and has lasted for the patient, and he used poultices, cauterizations, plasters, ointments, and bandages, and especially if it had been cauterized with the single cauterization we described, and nothing benefited him from that, then look. Then if the patient's head is strong in its structure by nature, and was not weak, and he found a severe cold, cauterize another cautery slightly above that one. Then take hold of each horn of its head until the thickness of the skin goes away and the bone becomes visible, as we have described. And take hold gently at the back of the head in the place known as the hatchet and lessen your hand in this one, and do not expose the bone because the patient will find for it a severe pain unlike the pain of all the other parts of the head and I shall mention this incision in its place.
The cautery that is used to cauterize the horns of the head and its back should be milder than the cautery that is used for the middle of the head, and this is its image.
Chapter Three.
In which [type] of headache  that is not chronic.
If pain occurs in the split of the head with a headache and the pain extends to the eye, then purge the patient with medicines that purify the head and use all the treatment that I have mentioned in the classifications of diseases. If this does not help, cauterize it on both sides. Either cauterize with a sharp, burning medicine or with iron.
As for cauterization with a burning medicine, take one clove of garlic, peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides, then make an incision in the place of pain on the temple with a wide scalpel until there is a space under the skin that can hold the clove.
Then place it under the skin until it disappears, then pull on it with a firm and tight tug, leaving it for about fifteen hours, then remove it and take out the garlic and leave the wound for two or three days, then carry on.
Upon it place cotton soaked in butter until the place is cauterized, then treat it with ointment until it heals, God willing. And if you wish, do this with some of the burning medicines that I have mentioned in the eighteenth article on burning medicines.
As for cauterization with iron, it is done in this manner: the iron implement whose figure is as follows:
And it is called the nail-shaped cautery because its head resembles a nail, with some holes in it and a small protuberance in the center.
Then, it is placed on the site of pain and you hold it with your hand while turning the iron slightly, and the amount burned from the thickness of the skin should be like half of it. And you raise your hand so as not to burn the vein that is below, and bleeding occurs, then you soak cotton in salt water and place it on the site and leave it for three days. Then you cover the cotton with ghee and treat him with ointment until he heals, God willing.
And if you wish,  you can burn this wound with the sharp edge coming from the cautery and preserve it from cutting the vein in this non-chronic wound especially.
Chapter Four.
Cauterizing a chronic wound.
If you treated the wound with what we mentioned from the previous treatments and what we mentioned in the sections of diseases, and the treatment did not work, and you saw from the cause what cannot be treated by what we mentioned of the first cauterization with medicine or cauterization with fire. Then it is necessary to cauterize the nail-shaped cautery until it becomes white after having learned on the site of pain in a line whose length is half a finger or so, and leave your hand once while pulling it until the vein is cut and reaches near the bone.
Except that you must be careful not to touch the jawbone that moves when chewing, so it burns the muscle or nerve that moves it and causes stiffness.
And be careful and cautious of bleeding from the vein you cut, for there is danger in cutting it. And especially for one who does not know what he is doing and has no experience in the practice and abandoned work is better.
And will come the mention of arranging for blood flow from the artery on its face in its place from the book, if God wills, and if you see from the cause what this kind does not accomplish.
And you saw the body of the sick person covered with a boil like this kind in the middle of the head as we described and treated the wound until it heals if God wills.
And if you wish, you used the kind that we mentioned in the chapter of piercing the artery with the iron tool having two blades, for it is a better and more effective kind than this.
The Fifth Chapter.
In the kind of ear aches.
If pain occurred in the ear from cold and treated with laxatives and all other treatment that we mentioned in the division, and the pain did not go away, then grasp the iron tool called the point whose image is this.
Then prick with it after heating it around the ear entirely as they rotate or all around them if the pain is in both. And move away with the kind from the root of the ear a little after you have learned the location with the lead pencil and the kind should be the amount of ten points in each ear or thereabouts, then treat the places until it heals if God wills.
The Sixth Chapter.
In the kind of abscesses.
The abscess that is treated with the kind is only the one that happens from phlegm as mentioned in the divisions of diseases.
And it avoids the kind that happens from boils and tightening of the nerve.
When you treated this kind of abscess with poultices and cupping and gargling and your treatment was not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize the sick person with three kinds. One is at the root of the ear and the second slightly below the notch and the third at the junction of the lips.
Make your position opposite to the diseased side because relaxation occurs in the side that appears healthy.
And the shape of the support is to mold it as a support opposite the upper corner of the ear slightly under the parietal bone and another in the temple, and its length should be equal to the length of the thumb.
Lower the support with your hand until it burns to about half the thickness of the skin, and this is the shape of the cautery, which is a type of knife that has advanced in its image but is slightly gentler than it, as you see. It should be slightly thicker at the edge of the knife, then treat the place as previously mentioned until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Seven.
In  chronic stroke.
If you treated the stroke and treated it with what we mentioned, but your treatment did not benefit, and there was no fever in the sick person, make four supports. On each horn of his head a support and a support in the middle of the head as we mentioned, and a support at the back of the head as previously mentioned.
The description of the cautery as previously mentioned, and it can also cauterize a support on the mouth of the stomach, which is more effective, then treat as previously mentioned.
Chapter Eight.
In forgetfulness.
The one who is caused by phlegm should be given the patient first with large herbs and brain-purifying pills.
Then shave his whole head, and carry on the back of his head a mustard poultice written in the article of the poultice, carry it several times because it is a type of support.
And do it on the same order that I mentioned there, if he is cured by that, otherwise, make three supports at the back of his head, aligned from the top of the head to the bottom of the neck.
Make between every band and band a thickness of a finger, then treat the sore as mentioned before.  If you wish to increase it and the patient is able for it, add the middle band.
If you wish to increase it, add on to the two horns then treat it until it heals, and the pad will be olive-shaped as shown previously.
The Ninth Chapter.
In paralysis and relaxation of the whole body.
It is necessary that you proceed in purifying the head with the poultices and what we have mentioned, then shave the patient's head, then add a band in the middle of the head and a band on each horn of the head and a band on its back.
And three on the vertebrae of the neck, if in a case of relaxation of the body you need more than that and the patient is able for it and the disease is strong and stubborn, add four bands on the vertebrae of his back. And make the band hot until it burns most of the skin and raise your hand then treat him as mentioned before until it heals, God willing, and the pad will be olive-shaped.
The Tenth Chapter.
In epilepsy.
Only the epileptic who has epilepsy from before phlegm is treated, so it is necessary that his nose be purified first with the large poultices and all the treatment mentioned in the division if the patient is large and able to take medicine.
But if he is a child who cannot bear medicine, then let him use gargles and the cleanser that purifies the brain before that for many days with improving his nourishment.
Then shave his head and add one band in the middle of the head as mentioned before in the description and another band on its back. And on each horn of his head, a band. If the patient is strong and able, add the bands mentioned in the case of paralysis and relaxation of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back, and the pad will be olive-shaped as described previously.
If the patient is a child, make the cauterizing iron gentle in this way.
The eleventh chapter.
On the treatment of melancholy.
If the cause of melancholy is putrid humors and thick phlegm, apply the cauterizations we mentioned in the treatise on apoplexy.
If the cause of melancholy is black bile and the body of the patient is moist and putrid, purge his nose as described previously in the division.
Then shave the patient's head and make a firm cake of cotton like a circle, then place it in the center of his head with the patient sitting upright holding onto each side, then take one ladleful of old sheep fat.
Then heat it on the fire at a moderate heat, as much as the finger can bear if inserted, then pour it in the center of his head in the circle and leave it until it cools. Do this to the patient every week once with all his good care until he heals, if God wills.
And if you wish, cauterize it with small dots without holding the cautery in your hand, but be a  light touch; this type of cauterization moistens the brain moderately.
Then put cotton soaked in sheep fat or chicken fat on top of it.
The twelfth chapter.
On the cauterization of water flowing in the eye.
If you notice the beginning of water flowing in the eye with the signs mentioned in the division, immediately purge the patient's head and protect him from all moisture and sweat him in the bath on an empty stomach for days.
Then shave his head and cauterize in the center of the head, then cauterize two on the temples if the beginning of water flowing in the eye is in both eyes or from one side if it is in one eye.
Then cut with the knife all the veins and arteries under the skin, and let the cauterizations be long in width across the temples, and take care that there is no bleeding.
If you see something of it, cut it at its place with any treatment that is possible for you, and we shall come to the wisdom in closing up arteries and cutting them and taking care that there is no bleeding.
And two good cauterizations may be made on the back of the head under the bones.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
On Chronic Blepharorrhagia.
If the tears of the eye are chronic and constant, and they are from the veins and arteries which are on the outside of the head from outside the head, and you are convinced that this is from a cold phlegm thick like boiling water, then cauterize as I have described before at the beginning of the water flowing down. Cauterize in the middle of the head and two on the temples, and two on the back of the head under the bones, and if you need to increase it, cauterize in each side of the base of the eye at the edge of the eyebrow with a small knife.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing a Smelly Nose.
If you treated it with what we have mentioned in the division and the treatment did not work, then hasten to prescribe the sick person three nights of cupping, then shave his head and cauterize the middle one with an olive oil knife. Then cauterize with the nail-shaped knife two on the eyebrows above the hair a little, and take care of the artery, do not cut it, and this is the shape of the nail-shaped knife.
The Fifteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing a Drooping Eyelid.
If the eyelid droops because of disease or moisture, cauterize the eyelid with one cauterization using this crescent-shaped knife.
If you wish, place two little lines above the eyebrows on each side, a little distance from the temples, and let the length of each line be equal to the length of the eyebrow.
Do not exaggerate your hand with the lines, but only as much as a third of the skin is burned, and the image of the iron will be like this.
The Sixteenth Chapter.
Lines on the Eyelid.
If its edges turned inward, so as to close in on the eye, then the lines within it are of two types. Either the lines with fire, or the lines with a burning medicine; as for the lines with fire, you must order the sick person before this to leave his lashes if he is one of those who pluck them until they grow long and even.
If they are plucked while growing, then bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they grow and become even. And if they have grown and become even, place the head of the patient in your block, then trace on the eyelid with lead a mark in the shape of a sheet of paper (i.e., a thin line).
And the beginning of the mark is near the lashes, then place under the eyelid cotton soaked in egg white or in the saliva of the lizard (i.e., a type of gecko), then heat the iron with this image.
Then cauterize on the shape which you have traced, little by little in many times until the surface of the skin which is like the shape of a sheet of paper burns entirely; its appearance is special and a sign that your work is correct is to see the eyelid become blackened and the hair rise above the lining of the eye.
Then raise your hand at that time and leave him for three days, then apply cotton soaked in butter to it until the scab falls off, then treat it with ointment until it heals if God wills. If something of the hair returns after some time and the eyelid relaxes.
Then return the eyelid to its place as you did before. If the hair is in the lower eyelid, it must be removed until it returns to its natural place and does not injure the eye. As for the cauterization with a burning drug, tell the patient to leave the incisions until they grow long and even.
Then you make from the paper a picture of a sheet of parchment, and take from the usual soap and from unslaked lime, from each one weight of a dinar or thereabouts. You grind them both very finely, and do this quickly so that it does not dry out. Then you spread it on the paper that you made in the likeness of a sheet of parchment, and place it on one or both eyelids, and put under the eye cotton soaked in egg white, and the head of the patient in his block.
And you place your index finger above the medicine and press it gently, and move it whenever the patient feels a prickling sensation from the medicine because he will feel a burning sensation like fire. As long as he feels the tingling sensation, leave the medicine and move it with your finger. If the tingling sensation subsides, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And look, if you see that the eyelid has risen as it rises when exposed to fire or cutting, otherwise, apply the medicine again on the place where the medicine did not affect and did not darken until you complete your work and the eye is cauterized. Then, place cotton with ghee on top of it until it removes the sting of burning.
Then, treat it with the palm ointment or other ointments until it heals. And it is necessary for you when working to be extremely careful that nothing of the medicine falls into the eye. If the eyelid relaxes after days and we fear something from the hair falling into the eye.
Then apply the medicine again on that place where the eyelid relaxed, especially as you did before, and then treat it until it heals. And this is a picture of a sheet of parchment.
Know that the eyes of people differ in size and magnitude, so according to this let your cupping be, and it is not a hidden way for him who has practice in this craft.
The seventeenth chapter.
Of the kind of tumor that appears at the corner of the eye.
If you treated the tumor with what we mentioned in the classifications of diseases and your treatment was not successful, it is necessary to cauterize it in this manner.
Order the patient to place his head in a block and have a servant hold his head between your hands, holding it so that it does not move or strike against his head.
Then place cotton moistened in egg white or the saliva of the barzquta on his eyes, then heat the cauterizing iron whose image is this.
It should be hollow like the form of an eagle's feather from one end which is where the cauterizing takes place, and if you wish it to be perforated at the other end, and if you wish it to be solid like a rod, except that this hollowing is better for your work, God willing.
Then, squeeze the tumor if it is open and remove its pus and dry it or if it is not open, open it and extract its discharge, then when you do this, place the cauterizing iron on it while it is very hot, hold it with your hand until it reaches the bone.
And withdraw your hand slightly at the cauterizing from the eye toward the nose so that your hand does not err or make the patient uneasy and the cauterizing iron falls into the cornea, thus spoiling it. If it reaches the bone in the first cauterization, otherwise, reheat the cauterizing iron a second time if you need to do so.
Leave him for three days, then apply cotton soaked in butter and treat him with the drying ointment until it heals. If forty days have passed and it has not healed, apply the severe medicine to burn until the bone is exposed and leave it as will be mentioned in its chapter, God willing.
Another method for treating a nasal discharge that some of the earlier surgeons have mentioned, is to cut into the site of the nasal discharge, then place a thin probe in the same incision. This is its image.
And pour into it a weight of a silver dirham melted lead, and hold your hand on the probe tightly firmly and steadily, so that the patient does not move at all lest the melted lead spill into his eye. And it is necessary to place on the eye of the patient cotton moistened in egg white or water.
For the lead burns the site of the nasal discharge and purifies it with a wonderful cure. If the nasal discharge is cured by what has been mentioned of cauterization and treatment, otherwise there is no need to use a nostril piercing and returning the nasal discharge to its nasal passage as will be mentioned in its more specialized place.
The Eighteenth Chapter.
In cauterizing a cleft lip.
A cleft lip is frequently found, called "the whisker," especially in the lips of boys, for it happens very often. If this cleft is treated with what has been mentioned in the previous section and the treatment was not successful, then take a small iron tool like a knife and heat it up as shown in the picture.
Its hollow should be like the sharpness of a knife, then place it forcefully in the cleft until the cauterization reaches the depth of the cleft and then treat it with the  "al-qiyurati" (a type of plaster) until it heals, God willing.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
In cauterizing the nasal discharge that occurs in the mouth.
If it appears in the root of the gums or in the palate or in the roots of the teeth, a tumor then bursts and becomes a discharge from pus. If it is treated and the treatment was not successful, then you must heat an iron tool to a degree suitable for the nasal discharge.
Then you introduce a shield into the hole of the nail and hold your hand until the iron, shielded, reaches its pit and its end, and you do this once or twice then treat him afterwards with what we have mentioned of the treatment until he is healed if Allah wills.
If the material was cut off and healed, otherwise it is necessary to expose the place and remove the decayed bone according to what will come in its chapter if Allah wills.
Chapter Twentieth.
On how to treat loose and loosened incisors.
If the gums loosened because of moisture and the incisors moved, and you treated them with medicines and they did not benefit, put the head of the patient in your stone and then heat the iron that comes with its image after this after you have placed the tube on the tooth.
And introduce the iron shielded quickly and hold your hand a little until the patient feels the heat of the fire reached the root of the tooth, then raise your hand and then return the iron several times as much as you want, then the patient fills his mouth with salt water.
And he holds it for an hour and spits it out, and the loosened tooth becomes fixed and the loose gums tighten and the harmful moisture dries up.
Chapter Twenty-First.
On how to treat toothache.
If the toothache is from the cold or there is a worm in it and the treatment with medicines did not benefit, then its treatment comes in two ways: either the treatment with butter or the treatment with fire.
As for the treatment with butter, it is that you take the cow butter and boil it in an iron ladle or a saucer, then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of the rod and dip it in the boiled butter and place it on the aching tooth quickly and hold it until it cools.
Then you return it repeatedly until the strength of the fire reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish to immerse a cloth or cotton in cold fat and place it on the aching tooth and place the protected iron above it until the fire reaches the bottom of the tooth.
As for cauterizing it with fire, you should resort to a copper pipe or an iron pipe that has some thickness so that the heat of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient, then hold the hot instrument whose image comes and place it on the same tooth and hold your hand until the instrument cools, do this repeatedly.
For the pain goes away either that same day or the next, and it is necessary after this cauterization that the patient fills his mouth with good fat and holds it for an hour then spits it out, and this is the image of the instrument.
Cauterize with any side you wish and on the measure you can, and this is the image of the pipe.
The Second Twenty-Second Chapter.
On Cauterizing Pigs.
If the pigs are from phlegm and cold humors and do not respond to ripening with medicine and you want rapid ripening, then heat the hollow instrument whose image comes here, its ends penetrating.
So that smoke comes out from the other end during cauterization, place it protected on the same tumor once and twice if you need to until it reaches the depth of the tumor, and if the tumor is small, make the instrument equal to the size of the tumor.
Then leave it for three days and carry on it a cloth soaked in fat until what was burned by the fire goes away, then treat it with ointment and threads until it heals, God willing.
The Third Twenty-Third Chapter.
On Cauterizing Hoarseness of Voice and Shortness of Breath.
If the humors prevail over the windpipe, especially if this is accompanied by a cold temperament, it becomes necessary for the patient to be first purged with laxatives, then to have a poultice applied at the notch of the throat at the root of the larynx in the lower position.
Beware that you do not bring the poultice to the larynx, nor burn from the skin except half of it, then apply another poultice at the articulation of the neck in the last bead of it, and make the compress stapled as in the manner mentioned before.
Then treat him with what has been mentioned before until he is healed, God willing.
The Twenty-Fourth Chapter.
On a poultice for a disease of the lungs and cough.
If the cough and lung disease are from cold humors and the patient has no fever nor dropsy, and the disease is chronic, apply two poultices on the upper sides of the collarbones in the low, soft, vacant spots and another poultice in the middle of the chest between the breasts.
And make the compress stapled as in the manner mentioned before, and if you wish, let your poultice be a drop with the compress called the point, and whose image was previously mentioned in the treatment of earache, and it consists of thirty points or thereabouts.
Then treat him with what has been mentioned before until he is healed, and you can make a compress of three branches in this manner, and it hastens the application of the poultice because you apply three poultices at once with it, and this is the image of the compress.
The Twenty-Fifth Chapter.
On a poultice for the armpit.
If the head of the humerus has dislocated due to slippery humors or it did not stay firm when it was returned from its dislocation until it became customary for it to be displaced and return again with even the slightest movement, as we have seen, then it is necessary to first set the jaw. Then the patient lies on his back or on his right side, and then you raise the skin inside the armpit with your left hand fingers if the joint is dislocated inwards.
Then you heat the two-footed iron as shown in its picture.
Then you cauterize the skin with it until it pierces to the other side and the shape of the cautery is four cauterizations, and it may be cauterized with an iron that has three heads, so the shape of the cautery then becomes six cauterizations and the heads are on the strength of the one who brings it.
And this is a picture of the three-headed iron.
And one may be added to this number so that the cauterizations become eight, then it is carried on the cauterized repeatedly with salt, then the patient is given rest and does not move the limb for a time until it strengthens, and if the dislocation is upward and rarely does that happen.
So it is cauterized above the shoulder one cautery good or many cauterizations in drops for the joint becomes firm and the moisture goes away and the patient heals.
Chapter twenty-sixth.
On Cauterizing the Stomach.
If there is in the stomach a cold and much moisture until it brings it out of its temper and the discharges increased to it and was treated with various treatments but did not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient lie on his back and stretch his legs and arms, then cauterize him three times. One cautery under the chest spoon, a finger's width with a pointed iron and two cauterizations below its sides of the one cautery until the shape of the cauterizations becomes triangular and further apart between them so that they do not converge if they are burned and the depth of the cautery is one-third the thickness of the skin and the shape of the cauterizations.
In this picture and to this extent no more.
And if you wish, sew it as one large piece in the middle of the stomach as shown in this picture.
And the iron used to sew this single patch should be circular as shown in this picture.

Chapter Twenty-Seven.
In a patch for a cold liver.
If the liver presents pain from coldness and dampness or from hot air until it has departed from its natural constitution excessively, and the sick person was treated with what was mentioned in the division, and that did not benefit him. And after each patch, it should be the thickness of a finger, and the patch should be straight along the body and do not clamp your hand with the iron yes.
And let the amount that is burned from the thickness of the skin be half, no more, and the sick person should stand on his feet; if he cannot stand, let him lie down with his legs extended and his arms raised, and this is a picture of the iron.

Chapter Twenty-Eight.
In a tumor of the liver with a patch.
If a fistula appears in the liver and you want to know if that tumor is in the liver flesh or in its peritoneum, if it is in the liver flesh, the patient will feel heaviness and pain without sharpness.
And if it is in the peritoneum of the liver, there will be severe pain along with sharpness and you will see that physicians have been unable to treat it. It is necessary for the patient to lie on his side then learn about the location of the tumor with ink.
Then heat the iron in the fire, and this is the iron that resembles a hoe, and here is its image. And shape it with one incision until it burns all the skin and reaches the peritoneum, so that the entire abscess comes out, then treat it with the treatment of fistulas until it heals.
And this type of incision should not be used by anyone except one whose experience in medicine is long and who has repeatedly treated these diseases with his own hands, so that he then undertakes such work, and leaving it to me is better.
Chapter Twenty-Nine.
On the Incision of Fistula in the Testicles.
The ancients described the incision of a cold testicle fistula as follows: take one long, dry root of ziraunond, as thick as a finger, and immerse it in oil and heat it in the fire. Then shape it with one incision between the connection of the collarbone and the neck, and two small incisions a little below the underarms, slightly slanted towards the side below the beard, and two large incisions above the breasts, between the third and fourth ribs.
And two incisions also between the fifth and sixth ribs, slanted slightly backward, and one incision in the middle of the chest and another above the stomach, and three incisions from behind, one between the shoulders and two on the sides of the spine below the incision that is between the hands.
It is not fitting that your hand goes deep into the abscess, but it should be a probing at the skin's surface. Some of the ancients mentioned that there are people who use an iron tool like a curved sword and heat it and insert it between the ribs until they reach the tumor itself.
And the pus comes out as we mentioned in the case of a liver abscess, and from this probing into an abscess, either the patient dies within the hour or a festering sore is exposed in its place that does not heal.
Chapter Thirty.
On Abscesses of the Spleen.
If you treated the spleen illness with what was mentioned of treatment in the previous division and your treatment did not work, then probing it is done in three ways, all of them correct. One of them is to probe it three or four times in a row along the length of the spleen.
In the shape of probes for the liver, as depicted and described earlier, with a space between each probe equal to or slightly more than the thickness of a finger. The quality of the probe should be as mentioned in the probing of the liver. Do not delve deeply with the probe, and the patient lies on his back.
The other method is in the armpit. Lift the skin opposite the spleen where the patient's left arm ends, and lift the skin opposite the spleen where the patientâ€™s right arm ends.  Raise the skin across the width of the body so that the probes fall along the length of the body.
Then, insert the three probes, very carefully, until they penetrate the skin from the other side, and then withdraw the probe, making four probes in total. If you wish, you can probe with the other probe, the one with the three heads.
Then treat the site of the probing after leaving it to drain pus for many days, as this is more effective than all other treatments mentioned before.
Chapter Forty-one.

And another cauterization on the liver and one on the spleen, and two behind his back between the vertebrae, one in front of his chest and another in front of his abdomen, and the depth of the cauterization should be close to the thickness of the skin, then the cauterization is left open to drain the pus for a long time.
And do not leave the patient without treatment after cauterization with what is necessary to bring together the interested parties so that he may recover quickly, and the picture of the iron that is used to cauterize the back is as described before and the one that is used to cauterize the back is olive-colored.

Chapter fifty-third.

Chapter Thirty-Six.
Of the cauteries that are in the buttocks and its environs.
If the ailment does not respond to the incision and the treatment we have described in its place, perhaps it will heal with cauterization. Then know the depth of its cavity with the probe, then take the cautery which resembles a pointed instrument and insert it heated into the same boil on a straight line with the direction of the boil's cavity and the depth that the probe entered, and repeat the cauterization until all those foul substances are burned once or twice or thrice, according to your need.
And beware of burning a nerve if there is one or a large vein, and if the boil leads to the bladder or the intestines.
So beware of all these locations, and only do this if the boil is in a fleshy location and you have judged that it is not infected. Then treat the area until it heals. If the area closes up and the materials are cut off from it and it remains so for a while, know that it has healed completely.
And if the materials are not cut off from it, know that it is infected or that there is a rotten bone or something similar to it in its cavity, which will be mentioned in its place.

The Fortieth Chapter.

Chapter Forty-One
Concerning Sciatica.
If pain occurs in the buttock and its cause is cold and moisture, and the patient was treated with what was mentioned in the classification and the treatment did not work, and time passed, then it becomes necessary to ease the patient from the thick humors by a poultice of henbane or a poultice of spurge and the like.
Then, apply a poultice and place the  treatment on two blows, either by using burning drugs or by cauterization with fire, and cauterization with fire is done in many ways; one of them is to cauterize three times on the buttock itself, like this.
And it should have a good depth, and the space between each cauterization should be the thickness of a finger, and the cauterizing instrument should be olive-shaped; and one may cauterize once in the middle on top of the hip itself, making four cauterizations. And if you wish, cauterize with the circle which was mentioned before in the cauterization for treating the hip, one cauterization.
So that the circle encircles the whole hip and burns all the thickness of the skin, this is the characteristic of cauterization for sciatica if the pain is persistent in the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
But if it extends to the thigh and leg, cauterize two times on the thigh at the place indicated by the patient where he feels pain, and one time above the ankle four fingers' width towards the outer side, slightly, and the cauterizing instrument should be flat and thin, and the depth of the cauterization should be equal to the thickness of the skin only.
And if he indicates that the pain extends towards the toes of the leg, cauterize where he points to you with a point instrument three or four times or more if it is necessary. And if he indicates the pain below the knee towards the leg, cauterize there one time, flat and thin.
Be careful in all your incisions that you do not reach a nerve or large artery, for this will result in a serious and painful ailment to the patient.
And I have seen one and another who was cauterized above the ankle and a cut was made in the incision, so that the leg became swollen until it reached the foot and it ulcerated all over and rotted the whole leg, then diarrhea occurred and death followed afterwards. If the pain is on both sides, cauterize both sides in the same manner.
And some wise men have mentioned in the incision of the hip, that it should be made like a cup made of iron, with its diameter half a cubit and at its mouth, a thickness of a date pit or a little less, and inside this cup there is another cup and a third.
And what is between each cup should be the size of a thumb joint, and the cups should be open on both sides and their height should be about one or two joints and they should take handles from iron well-fixed in the cups and this is its form.
Then it is heated in the fire until it becomes red-hot and throws sparks, then it is placed on the hip of the patient and the patient leans on his healthy side so that three round incisions are made in one go, then he is left for three days and cauterized with butter and the wound is left open for several days.
Many times, then it is treated with ointment until it heals. The author of this book said that this type of incision is rarely used because of its difficulty, its bad appearance, and the few people who can endure it, except that it is a good incision for those who endure it and suffer from it in its place.
As for the incision with burning medicines, it is to make two cups like the throat of a chalice in which a reed pipe made of copper or iron descends.
Its sides should have a height of two joints or so, and what is between them should be the thickness of a finger, and it should be open at the bottom and closed at the top, and some parts are held together like this form.
Then bring it down upon the hip and place the afflicted person lying on his healthy side, pressing your hand firmly. Then pour between the two circles of the sharp water, which is heated by the brazier, and hold it for a Roman hour. The afflicted person endures its sweetness and burning; he feels a burning like fire.
Until the burning subsides, then raise your hand with the instrument and wipe the sharp water from the entire hip with fresh water. Then leave it for three days and apply butter to it until the blackness of the burn disappears. Leave it for days until pus flows from it, for this is more beneficial.
Then treat him with ointments until he heals. If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make a mold for him similar to what was made for the hip, holding water in it according to the same method as for the hip. This is the description of the sharp water, and I have established it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines.
Take from the salt of the kidney and from unquenched quicklime, one part each, grind them together, and put them in a new pot that has been pierced at the bottom with a small hole equal to what the water enters. Put another pot under the bottom of the pot, filled with water.
And pour on the kidney and quicklime fresh water, enough to cover them with a finger after you have pressed them well with your hand. Leave the pot until the sharp water descends into the bottom pot filled with water, then collect all of that water and pour it on other quicklime and kidney, renewing them again.
For it becomes then very powerful, effective in many medical procedures and for treating all kinds of ailments because it acts like fire itself. And there are medicines that also cauterize the hip with it such as the thaphsia, honey from the  bladders (?), and quicklime mixed with soap steeped in vinegar.
And Galen claimed a story about an ancient man who treated hip pain and sciatica, exaggerating its importance greatly and claiming that it didn't need any other treatment and that it healed with a single application.
Even perhaps he may enter the bath carrying it and come out cured, which is to take from the green shistrj, if the green is not found, then take the recent dry one and finely pound it with some tallow and place it on the hip where the pain is, or in the leg or in the thigh.
And tighten it and leave for three hours or as much as the patient feels the burning subside, then put him in the bath, if his body is softened, then put him in the basin, because the pain goes away and he is healed by God's permission, if he doesn't heal, repeat the poultice after ten days once more.
For he is healed if God wills, and know that it is not proper for anyone to use these remedies except after emptying the body, and Dioscorides mentioned that goat's milk whey when applied as a compress to sciatica was beneficial from it.
And the cautery should be like this, take wool and soak it in old oil and place it on the deep place that is between the thumb of the hand and the cubit, which is closer to the cubit, then take dried goat's whey.
Then ignite it with fire until it becomes embers, then place it on the wool and leave it until it goes out, then take another one and do not stop doing this until the feeling reaches from the middle of the arm to the hip and the pain subsides by God's permission, and this type of cautery is called the goat's whey cautery.

On Cauterizing Back Pain.

It should be cauterized with a point, and if you wish, cauterize it three or four times with a medium-sized nail iron according to this picture.
The Third Chapter.
In cauterizing the beginning of the hump.

The Fourth Chapter
In cauterizing gout and joint pain.
If the pain in the joints is from cold dampness that flows into any member of the body, then if the pain occurs in the legs, it is customary for physicians to call it gout specifically.
So if the cold gout is treated with the types of treatment mentioned in the division and the pain does not go away, then cauterization removes it, which is to cauterize after emptying around the joint of the leg many times, and the iron should be medium-sized olive on this picture.
