The Fifth Forty Chapter.
On Cauterizing a Hernia.
If a hernia appears in the groin and some of the intestines and peritoneum have descended into the testicle and it is newly formed, it is necessary to order the patient to abstain from food for the day and use emollient medications that help evacuate stool from his abdomen.
Then have him lie between your hands on his back and order him to hold himself until the peritoneum or intestines protrude, then return it with your finger and learn with the lead pencil under the hernia on the pubic bone a mark resembling half a circle with its ends towards the upper part of the body.
Then cauterize this shape with a hot iron.
Until it turns white and throws sparks, then return the intestines or peritoneum into his abdomen, and let a servant place his hand on the spot so that the intestines do not protrude. Also, loosen between the patient's legs and place a cushion under him and another servant tie around his legs.
And another one on his chest holding his hands, then bring the hot iron down on the same mark and your hand with the iron standing straight, and hold it until it reaches the bone or apply it again if it does not reach the bone the first time.
Take care to avoid the intestines protruding while you cauterize them lest you burn them and thereby cause the patient either death or a great affliction. Know that if you do not cauterize deeply enough, your work will be unsuccessful. And it is necessary for the iron of the youth to be gentle on their bodies and for the elderly on theirs.
Then treat the cauterized area after three days with butter until the marks of the fire disappear, then treat it with all other ointments until it heals. Let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
It is necessary to make his diet during treatment the following:  to keep his belly full so that the intestines do not protrude when he moves or strains himself. Then, if he wants to get up after forty days, use a tight bandage and hold it for another forty days, reducing exertion and fullness from food and drink, and loud shouting.
For if he uses this method thus, he will heal completely, God willing. I will mention the treatment of inguinal hernias in its chapter, God willing. As for the hernia that occurs in the rest of the abdomen and is just beginning, if you want it not to increase, cauterize the hernia with a round iron according to its size. And let what you burn from the skin be like a third of it, then treat it with what we have mentioned, for it will not increase, God willing. Some of the ancients mentioned cauterizing the hernia with a triangular iron in this manner.
After you have learned to treat the hernia with cauterization, make a line with the pencil on the side of the top of the hernia and the other line towards the bottom, and lower your hand in the middle with one cauterizing iron. The first cauterization is easier and better, God willing.
Chapter Forty-Six.
On Cauterizing the Varices.
If a loss or blow occurs in some of the organs, and pain persists for a long time and does not yield to medicinal treatment, it is necessary that the point be cauterized with a hot iron, and each organ should be cauterized according to its size, whether large or small, weak or strong.
And if the pain and throbbing cease, then he is cured from the first cauterization; otherwise, it should be repeated upon him because these pains are accustomed to transfer from the organ to what is near it, so it is necessary to follow them with cauterization until the sick person heals.
The Forty-Seventh Chapter.
Cauterizing Leprosy.
As for those with leprosy, they may benefit greatly from cauterization, especially the type of leprosy that comes before the putrefaction of phlegm and blackening.
If you wish to cauterize a patient, if the leprosy is just beginning and you treated it with what was mentioned in the division and it did not improve and did not stop, and you fear that corruption will overcome his entire temperament, then cauterize five points on the head. One in the center of the head as usual, and the second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, two on the temples, and one from behind on the nape of the neck, and make your hand's cauterization slightly so that it affects the bone to a slight degree.
And remove scales from it so that breathing becomes easier for the thick steam, and cauterize it similarly on the same spleen as mentioned before. As for if leprosy has persisted in the patient and appeared clearly, then it is necessary to cauterize these points mentioned on the head. And cauterize one point on the tip of the nose, two points on the cheeks, two points on the cervical vertebrae, six on the dorsal vertebrae, one large one on the coccyx at the tailbone area and another above it in the same place, and two on the shins, one on each. Two on each knee, two on each ankle, two on each elbow, two on the armpits, and two on the joints of the fingers of his hands and feet, and on every heel of his legs and wrists of his hands.
And be cautious of the nerve on the back of the heels lest you burn them, and it may be cauterized at the pubic bone and another on the mouth of the stomach and another on the liver, and know that every time you increase cauterization it is more beneficial and better.
And know that the sick person does not feel pain from cauterization as the healthy person does because his body has become numb, and it is necessary that the cauterizations be large or small according to the organs and joints as mentioned previously in the descriptions of the instruments.
Then treat the cauterization with a fine poultice of honey and all other treatments until it heals, if God wills.
The Eighth Forty Chapter.
In cauterization of numbness, when a member from the members has been treated with medications and ointments and bandages but did not heal, cauterize the same numbed member with cauterizations according to what it deserves based on the size of the bone or smallness of the member and let your cauterizations be slightly thicker in the thickness of the skin.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals, and it may be cauterized for some numbness that appears in the hand or foot at the vertebrae of the back when the nerve that moves that member exits, so that the numbness goes away.
And do not proceed with this except one who is knowledgeable about the anatomy of the organs and exits of the nerves that move the body.
The Ninth Forty Chapter.
In cauterization of leprosy.
If leprosy has become chronic and no cure from the remedies of medicine has helped it, then cauterize on it with cauterizations a little depth according to the thickness of the skin until the whiteness goes away and its color changes.
Then, treat it with fine lentils with rose oil, the tongue of a lamb, and the blood of pigeons or doves, one part of each. Mix all together and apply it to a cloth and bind it to the place until it heals.
The Fiftieth Chapter.
Concerning cancer.
If cancer is just beginning and you want to stop it, burn it with a circular cauterizing instrument around it as it revolves. Some wise men have mentioned burning a blister in the center of it, but I do not see this because I expect that it will scald, and I have seen this happen several times.
So the right thing is to cauterize around it in a circle as we said, or with many cauterizing instruments.
The Sixty-First Chapter.
Concerning the treatment of ringworms.
If a ringworm has developed on someone and it is slow to mature, either because of the person's nature, or because of old age if he is weak in blood, or because of time, and you want to speed up the maturation of the ringworm, cauterize around it with many small cauterizing instruments that drip.
Then leave it, for it will speed up the maturation. If you want to cover it with a cauterizing instrument, take the cauterizing instrument whose image is shown here.
And lower it into the center of the ringworm until it penetrates the skin, and let the cauterizing instrument be from below so that the pus can flow easily, then treat it as appropriate until it heals.
The Seventy-Second Chapter.
Concerning the cauterization of ulcers.
An ulcer is a corruption that spreads in the body, eating it away like fire consumes dry wood. If you see an ulcer in a place where cauterization with fire is possible, take many small and large cauldrons, as appropriate for the place containing the ulcer.
Then take it from each side until the entire decay is removed and nothing of it remains at all, then leave it for three days and apply to the burned places powdered sulfur with oil until all scabs and all the decay are loosened.
Then treat it with healing ointments for the flesh. If, after three days, you see that the flesh is growing healthy growth without decay, otherwise, re-burn the remaining decayed areas, and the ulcer may be treated with a strong medicine.
For it is more effective than fire in healing quicker, and I have mentioned treating it with a strong medicine in the division, so take it from there whenever you need it.
The Thirty-Fifth Chapter.
On Burning Nails, Both Reversed and Unreversed.
This ailment often occurs in the soles of the feet, which is a rough thing that afflicts men, and burning it has two methods, either by fire or by hot water.
As for burning with fire, it is to heat a curved iron tool resembling an eagle's feather, made of iron according to the extent of the nail on all sides and having a thin edge, then place a hot protective layer on the nail and turn your hand with the tool around the nail until the tool reaches the depth of the nail.
And leave it for three days to be covered in pitch, then bandage it with pounded fine bread mixed with salt and leave the bandage on her overnight as it will loosen from its roots, and then treat the wound site with a healing ointment for the flesh until it heals, if the nails are not reversed.
And it often occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet, so you should take a tube of brass or iron or an eagle's feather, place it over the nail or wart, then pour a small amount of hot water into the tube.
Hold your hand and while turning it slightly, you cause the tube's edge to reach the screwâ€™s base, and the sharp water finds its way down to the screw's root and the patient endures for a little while the pain of the sharp water for a moment.
Then you leave it and the screw will come loose with its roots, thus do this one by one until you reach all that is in it within the body, then treat its places after it has been removed with what grows flesh from ointments.
Chapter Forty-Five.
In the case of a festering sore.
If a festering sore occurs from cold in the nerve or from a quarter fever or otherwise, it is necessary to make four or five poultices on the back of the spine between each bead and a poultice in its chest. And on his abdomen, a poultice with the olive oil iron, so that the festering sore settles and hastens the ripening of the cold illness.
Chapter Fifty-Five.
In the case of a bruise that occurs in the body.
A bad bruise may appear in the body, caused by cold, thick and rotten substances, so when it first appears, a gentle poultice should be applied on top of each sore with a stick whose end has been lit by fire or with the root of long saffron or with an eyeglass iron.
And the buboes may be poulticed at their first appearance in this way so that they do not increase and the effective power of the treatment fades away, and the patient recovers from it except that it is necessary to do this after the patient has been bled.
Chapter Sixty-Six.
In the case of bleeding that occurs when an artery is cut.
Bleeding often occurs from an artery that has been severed at a wound exposed from outside or when cutting a tumor or poulticing a member, etc., making it difficult to stop its flow.
If this happens to someone, hasten with your hand to the artery's mouth and place your index finger upon it and pull it tightly so that the blood is constricted under your finger and nothing comes out of it. Then put in the fire small and large olive-sized pieces of kindling and fan them until they become very hot.
Then take one, either small or large, according to the wound and the place where the artery burst open, and put the hot piece of kindling on the same vein after you hastily remove your finger and hold the piece until the blood stops.
If the blood rushes out when you raise your finger from the artery's mouth and the hot piece of kindling cools, take another hot piece quickly from the prepared kindling in the fire and keep doing this with one after another until the blood stops.
Be cautious not to burn the nerve that may be there so you would inflict another ailment on the patient, and know that if an artery bleeds from it, it cannot be cut, especially if it is a large artery, except in one of four ways: either by cauterization as we have mentioned, or by amputation if it has not already been amputated. For if it is amputated, its two ends contract and the blood stops, or it can be tied with strong thread, or medicine that stops bleeding and tightening with bandages tightly can be applied to it.
As for anyone who tries to cut it with a ligature or by tightening with cord, or by placing burning things and the like on it, it does not stop completely except rarely. If this happens to someone and there is no doctor or medicine available, he should hasten to put his index finger on the mouth of the wound as we have described.
And he should pull it tightly until the blood is constricted and it stops flowing from above the wound and on the artery, and the finger does not remove from it with cold water always, constantly until the blood solidifies and stops, and during that time, you look at what he needs of cauterization or medicine.
Chapter Two.
On incisions, ruptures, venesection and similar surgical procedures.
Al-Khalaf said: We have mentioned in the first chapter all illnesses that are treated with cauterization and corrosive medications, their causes and reasons, instruments, forms of cauterization, and made it sections from the top to the bottom.
And I follow in this chapter that same path so that it is easy for the student to obtain what they need...
Before I begin that, it is necessary for you, my sons, to know that this chapter contains more danger than what is in the first chapter about cauterization.
And because of that, the warning in it should be more severe because work in this chapter often involves the emptying of blood which is responsible for life when opening a vein or making an incision on a tumor, abscess, or to treat a surgery or remove an arrow or make an incision on a stone, and the like, all of which accompany danger and fear and most of them end in death.
And I advise you to avoid falling into what is dubious among you, for in this profession, many types of people with various illnesses may come to you, some of whom have been weakened by their illness and are close to death.
Because of the severity of their illnesses, and the length of their suffering, and the illness's indication of death, and some who exhaust their wealth to seek health from you with a promise of reward, and their illness is stubborn, it is not right for you to help anyone whose characteristics clearly show this.
And let your caution be stronger than your desire and eagerness, and do not proceed with anything of that unless you have certain knowledge about what will happen to the desirable outcome, and apply in all treatment of your illnesses, advancement of knowledge and warning about what leads to safety.
For in that, there is for you help in acquiring praise, glory, remembrance, and thanks. May God enlighten you, my sons, with guidance and not prohibit you from righteousness and success, indeed that is by His hand, there is no god except Him.
I have arranged this chapter into sections according to what came before in the chapter on wounds from the back to the front so that it would be easier for you to obtain what you want from it, God willing.
The First Section.
In Treating the Water That Collects in the Heads of Boys.
This ailment often afflicts boys at birth if the midwife squeezes the baby's head roughly, or it may occur from a hidden cause that is unknown.
I have not seen this ailment in anyone other than boys, and all that I have seen of them died quickly. Therefore, I saw it as best to leave treatment for it.  I have seen a boy whose head was full of water and his head grew larger every day. Until the boy could not sit on himself because of the size of his head, and the dampness increased until he died.
This dampness is either collected between the skin and bone or collected under the bone on the peritoneum, and the treatment for it if the dampness is between the skin and bone and the swelling is small is that you should make a single incision in the middle of the head lengthwise, about two finger-lengths long, until the dampness drains. This is the shape of the scalpel.
If the dampness is more and the swelling is greater, make it two incisions that intersect in this shape:
And if the dampness is under the bone and its sign is that you see the sutures of the head open from every side, and the water sinks when you press it with your hand inward, and this is not hidden from you, then it is necessary to make three incisions in the middle of the head in this shape.
After the incision, all of the dampness comes out, then you sew up the incisions with thread and dressings, then cover it from above with syrup and oil until the fifth day, then tie the bandage and treat the wound with ointment and pastes, do not leave the head binding too tight, and feed the patient with every dry food that is low in moisture.
Until the member is strong and healed, another prescription from incision: observe where the tumor bone appears and the gathering of water because it may be in the back of the head or in its front or on the right or on the left.
So it is meant by incision where the tumor appeared to you and the water filled, so you cut it as much as you can and be careful not to cut a vein so that bleeding occurs and the patient dies from that bleeding along with the expelling of moisture.
Chapter Two.
The cutting of the two veins behind the ears known as the jugulars.
When a severe ailment appears to the eyes or to the chest, and for that time there is no remedy with medicines, then the treatment in this case is the cutting of these two veins.
When you want to cut them, shave the head of the patient with the razor then rub the place with a rough cloth so that the vein appears, then tighten the neck of the patient by means of his garment and look where the sweat pulsates and their locations are the two low spots behind the ears, rarely concealed except in some people.
Then mark them with the stylus and cut them with the scalpel, cutting to the bone, that being the breadth of the head, and if you wish, insert the scalpel from below the vein and penetrate it upwards by cutting, making the length of the cut about two fingers clenched together.
For if the sweat is cut, blood will come out with a pulsating flow that reaches forward and backwards in a continuous stream. If the vein does not appear to the touch, then you should measure from the ear three finger lengths then mark it with the stylus and cut to the bone.
Send from the blood six awqats in the middle and perhaps you send more or less, all that depending on what appears to you from the strength of the patient and the fullness of his veins, then look at the wound if something of the peritoneum remains on the bone, cut it.
So that a hot tumor will not appear and the wound is tightened with a thread from coarse linen, and it is treated with ointments until it heals.
The Third Chapter.
Slitting the Arteries in the Wrists.
If a person experiences chronic sciatica or acute attacks due to hot humors and heat in the muscles of the wrists or severe chronic headache, and treatment with various medical methods has been ineffective, we have tried in these diseases slitting or cauterizing the arteries in the wrists as we described.
And the method of work in slitting them is to shave the hair on the wrists, meaning the superficial artery in the temple because it becomes apparent to you from its pulse and rarely is it hidden except for some individuals.
Or in case of severe cold if it is hidden from you, let the patient pull his head up with the help of his clothing, then rub the area with a cloth or cover the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly visible. Then take the scalpel whose picture is this. Then you gently slit the skin with it until you reach the artery, then insert a ligature into it and pull it upwards until it is brought out of the skin and freed from the membranes beneath it on all sides. If the artery is thin, twist it with the end of the ligature. Then cut a portion from it equal to the distance between its ends and it contracts without bleeding, for if it is not severed and cut, the blood will not stop at all, then drain the blood for six hours to three.
If the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it in two places with a strong doubled thread, and let the thread be either from abrism or from bowstrings, so that the decay does not hasten to it before the wound heals and bleeding occurs.
Then, cut the excess between the ligaments. Do this at that time or after a while. And if you want to mold it like bone with a knife, until its edges become blunt, then it will perform this work in itself or better as we have said.
Except if the patient has a fever or an imbalance in his temperament because cauterization helps to eliminate fluids, so it is more beneficial. It is also necessary after cutting the two arteries to fill the place with wool and put on compresses tightly. After healing, it should be treated with dry medicinal herbs that promote the growth of flesh and plaster until it heals, God willing.
If bleeding occurs from the artery during your work, quickly proceed to cut it either with cauterization or by filling the place with antimony and tightening your hand until the blood stops. If none of these are available to you, put your finger there until the blood clots.
Then, wash the place with very cold water until the pain subsides and tighten it as necessary.
And you bring it down firmly until it reaches the bone, and the sweat is cut in two places so that there may be a distance between its ends, for it does not fuse together with this kind at all, and this is the image of the iron.
The two blades of it should be sharp, resembling the two small pointed ones, except that they are much less sharp than a knife, because if they were as sharp as a knife, cold would reach them faster and the flesh would not be cut quickly;  and if there is some thickness in them, the heat will cling to them.
And flesh is cut quickly by it, and this work is better than all works, lighter and easier, and let there be after the two blades a thickness equal to the thickness of a finger.
Chapter Four.
In the treatment of hot and constant flow of tears from the eyes.
If the tears are constant and their flow is from the vessels on the skull's surface from the outside, and there is no benefit in treating it with medicines, and I see the face of the patient have reddened. And he feels in his forehead a prickling like the prickling of ants, and his eyes are sunken, wet, and the corners of them have been affected and their eyelids have become chafed from the intensity of tears; then they were forced in treating it to this work, and they call it treatment by the sword, which is that you order the patient to shave the hair on his forehead.
Then, you make three incisions on the forehead, parallel to each other along the length of the forehead, and the length of one incision is about two fingers;  the first one is parallel to the length of the nose in the middle of the forehead, the second one a little distance away from the movement of the muscle in the temple, and the third one on the opposite side.
And be careful not to cut the two arteries on the sides, and keep your hand away from the connection of the jaws;  and let there be after each incision a distance of three fingers compressed, and let it be with you a piece of sponge prepared or many dry cloths for absorbing blood.
Then you insert the pointed double-edged knife, whose image is this. From the incision following the temple to the middle incision and with it you dissect all the skin that is between the incisions, along with the peritoneum on the bone, then do this also from the middle incision to the third incision, then you withdraw this knife. And you insert into the first incision another instrument called a sharp-edged  one on one side and rounded, not sharp on the other, and this is its image:
And you make its sharp side toward the flesh adhering to the skin and its rounded side toward the bone, and you push it until it reaches the middle incision and with it cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes without the cut reaching the outside of the skin.
Then you do this in the middle incision to the other incision, and after a moderate amount of blood has flowed, you press on the sites from where the clotted blood is coming out, then you put a cotton thread soaked in vinegar water in each incision, and place a pad that has been drenched with wine and oil or vinegar and oil on top of it.
So that a hot tumor does not occur, and on the third day, the bandage is removed and a lot of warm water is used for rinsing, then it is treated with a salve of vaseline mixed with rose oil and everything else that surgical wounds are treated with until it heals, God willing.
The Fifth Chapter.
In the Treatment of Tears and Drippings to the Eyes from the Interior of the Head.
When one experiences a lot of acute, sharp, constant dripping and sees the eyes from it sunken and small, and his vision has weakened, and the eyelids are eroded, and the lashes have fallen out from them. And there is a sharp, painful ache deep in the head and a constant sneeze, so know from these symptoms that those materials and drippings come from many deep blood vessels, and the best treatment for this is this treatment, which is to order the patient to shave his forehead and then make one incision in the middle of the forehead. Chapter Six.
In treating what falls into the ear.
All that falls into the ear is one of four types: either a metallic or semi-metallic stone like iron and glass, or a vegetable particle like lentils, seeds, and the like, or something fluid like water, vinegar, and the like.
And if it is an animal, when a stone or kind of stone that does not easily enter the ear falls into it, receive the ear with sunlight. If you see the stone, put something of violet fat or cerium oil in it, then try to remove it by moving your head or using a cotton swab. And plug the nostrils when sneezing comes after you put a ring of cloth or wool around the ear and pull the ear upwards, as it often exits with this treatment. If it doesn't exit, then try to remove it with a soft cotton swab as shown in its image.
If it comes out with the swab, otherwise try to remove it with a soft, slightly bent blind probe. If it doesn't come out with that, then make a tube of copper and insert one end of the tube into the hole of the ear carefully.
Then plug around the tube with soft, greasy material so that air does not have a way out other than through the tube, then draw it out with your breath forcefully and repeatedly, and very often it will be drawn out this way. But if it is not drawn out as described above, then take a small amount of  the chewing gum of the Arabs or of the sharpened gum that birds use and put it on the end of the probe.
After it has been wrapped in tightly packed cotton, then insert it into the ear canal gently after the ear has dried from moisture, and if all that was described above does not come out, then immediately make an incision before a hot swelling or inflammation occurs.
The incision prescription is to first cut the patient's ear carefully and drain the blood from him according to its strength, then sit the patient between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small incision at the base of the ear near its fleshy part in the lower area.
And the incision should be crescent-shaped until you reach the stone, then remove it with whatever tools you can, and then stitch up the incision immediately and treat it until it heals.
And if the thing that fell into the ear is one of the beans that swell and inflate, try to remove it as described above. But if it does not yield to being removed, then take a thin, delicate scalpel like this.
And try to cut that type of bean that fell into the ear with it, but only do this if you are certain that the bean has been moistened by the ear's vapor until it becomes small pieces, then remove them with a blunt forceps or a soft swab or with suction.
As we mentioned, it is easy to remove them. And as for water entering the ear, it is necessary to use the patient's sneeze with a handkerchief first, and after his ear has been filled with some loose cotton while he is lying on that ear that has water, if it comes out by doing so.
Otherwise, take many small smooth pebbles and warm them slightly by fire, and insert one into the patient's ear hole and make him rest his leg on that side and strike the stone in the ear with another stone.
He should continue to do this with one stone after another until all the water comes out, and he may also bring it out by taking a reed or feather and inserting one end into the ear and heating the other end in fire until most of it burns, then replacing it with another feather.
Do this repeatedly until all the water comes out, or draw it out with a tube as mentioned before with the stone. As for removing any animal inside it, look: if it is small like a flea or similar, treat it as mentioned in the previous section, but...
if its body is large and can be felt, try removing it with a probe and tweezers. This is easier than all other things that may occur in the ear. As for removing a worm that has developed in the ear if you treated it as mentioned in the previous section on 'Earwax' and your treatment did not work...
then you should look into the ear in the sunlight: if something of the worm appears to you, remove it with a probe or tweezers carefully. If nothing appears to you, take a tube of this shape...
Narrow at the bottom and wide at the top, and insert the narrow end into the ear as much as the patient can tolerate, then suck on it with a strong pull. Do this repeatedly until all the worm comes out. If it does not come out, seal around the tube with wax as I mentioned to you with the stone.
If it does not come out with what has been mentioned, use the earwax as I have mentioned before, which was experimented with by the first healers to kill the worm and you will find that in the section on 'Earwax'. It is through this instrument that you pour medications into the ear: its shape is...
As you see, it is made from silver or brass, narrow at the bottom with a small hole, and wide at the top. And if you wish the plunger inside the tube to be of well-fitted brass, or if you wish, take a reed and wrap cotton tightly around its end.
Then you put the grease or juice or whatever you want of these medicines in the tube while it is in the ear, and then insert the reed with cotton from above and squeeze it with your hand moderately until the grease is driven into the middle of the hearing and feels.
With the sick person inside, and let what is poured into the ear have been warmed slightly in the fire, and beware that what is being dripped into it is not very cold or very hot, for the ear cannot tolerate that.
Chapter Seven.
In the Treatment of a Obstruction in the Ear.
Some children may be born from their mothers' wombs and their ear canals unpierced.
And some people may also suffer from a blockage in the ear canal due to an injury or a fleshy growth inside it, and this blockage may be deep within the ear canal beyond sight.
And some may be visible a little outside the opening, and it is seen. The one that appears deep inside the ear and cannot be seen is in most cases difficult to remove, and the one that is seen should put the patient's ear in the sun. And look into it, if you see the blockage visible, then open it with a gentle scalpel, and this is its shape:
Its tip has some slight curvature, and the rest of the scalpel is smooth on both sides so as not to harm the ear. If the blockage is due to flesh that has grown in the ear canal, grasp it with a gentle forceps and cut it gently until all the flesh is removed.
If the blockage is deep inside the ear, take a gentle, smooth wire, warm it slightly in the fire, then insert it into the ear canal. If you feel the blockage and the patient feels heaviness of hearing, move it gently.
Take precaution not to injure the ear nerve and then put a wick in the ear that is the size of the hole, having soaked it in Egyptian ointment, do this for days until you are sure the wound has healed or take a wick, wet it in water, and sprinkle powdered saffron on it.
And use it, and if you see the ear has swollen with a hot pus, it is necessary to remove the wick and replace it with another wick that has been soaked in rose butter until the swelling subsides, then treat her until she heals.
If bleeding occurs, soak a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use the rest of the treatment that stops the bleeding mentioned in the article on cauterization.
Chapter Eight.
In treating warts that appear in the eyelids.
These warts that appear in the eyelids may be wet or dry, so it is necessary to hold them with a tweezer or pliers and cut them with a scalpel from their roots, then apply powdered saffron to the place.
If it bleeds from them, cauterize it with a fine lentil iron and cover it best after cutting, and often they return if something remains of their roots, and if cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and they do not return.
Chapter Nine.
In treating the cold that appears in the eyelids.
Often, something resembling frost in its severity and rigidity appears in the eyelids.
And because of this, it is called frost, which is the gathering of thick moisture in the upper eyelid and the lower eyelid, and the action in it is to look if the frost appears prominent on the surface of the eyelid, moving in every direction, then its matter is easy, so make a slit in it lengthwise.
Then, I would gently dissect it from all sides until you are free of it, then hang it on the suture and cut it off. If it does not appear to you to be able to cut it off except after the eyelid has been cut by the incision, there is no harm to the patient. If the cut is large, gather it with stitching and treat it until it heals.
And if it is small, there is no harm in leaving it; the ointment will cover it and heal it. If the flap is tilted inwards towards the inner surface, turn the eyelid over and hang the flap with a suture without needing to make an incision, and cut it off from all sides.
If the eyelid has been cut by the incision, there is no harm in this. Then wash the eye after cutting the flap with salt water and treat the area with something that will heal it until the patient heals.
The Tenth Chapter.
In Treating a Stye That Appears in the Eyelid.
A sty is a swelling that occurs in the layers of the upper eyelid, and it most commonly affects children. It weighs down their eyes and causes them to have discharges in the mornings, and they are unable to look at sunlight. Because the tears hasten toward them.
And therefore you see them leaning on their faces always, and on it they sleep. Their eyelids are beneath their eyebrows, wet with a puffiness and swelling of the sty is visible to the eye. And when you press the area with your fingers, you feel the sty between them.  The work to be done is that the patient put his head in a basin.
Then take a linen cloth and prepare from it a wick, and make from that wick a circle the size of what encloses the sty on all sides, then place it on it and press with your fingers on all sides to gather the sty in the center of the circle.
Then make an incision in the middle of that moisture with the knife, a longitudinal incision and do not make it larger than the incision made in venesection. As for the depth, you must cut through all the skin until you reach the trachea.
And in most cases, the trachea protrudes from the incision in the form of a white fatty piece. So you draw it out with a cloth that you have wrapped between your fingers to the outside while you turn your hand right and left until it is separated. And beware of increasing the incision so that the knife does not touch the eye and harm it.
If the trachea does not appear to you in the first incision, it is necessary that you increase the incision a little gently until the trachea protrudes and then draw it out as we said. Then you dip a cloth in vinegar and water and place it on the location and hold it firmly. And some people crush salt.
And he puts it in the depth of the incision so that what remains of that moisture dissolves, then treat him until it is healed. If a hot tumor occurs at the location, treat it with a soothing poultice until it heals.
Chapter Eleven.
In Kinds of Eye Scurvy.
If growths appear in the eyelid, excessive eyelashes beyond the natural course under the natural lashes and they are constricted, then they harm the eye and cause some diseases such as continuous tearing, relaxation of the eyelids, whiteness, and thickening until it becomes a cause for blindness of the eye.
And eye scurvy in four ways, either by cauterization with fire or by a strong medicine as mentioned before in the chapter of cauterization, or that it may be by cutting and stitching or by reed as I will describe this.
It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your block and then turn the eyelid with your left hand, if it turns, otherwise, insert a needle into it with a thread from below the eyelid and penetrate the needle with the thread from above, and this should be near the hair itself, and draw the thread upward to the eyelid.
Turn it with the forceps and then make an incision in the inner part of the eyelid without the excessive hair, with a scalpel, from the larger canal to the smaller canal. Then loosen the thread and place under the eyelid a small pad of cotton or linen and then learn on the eyelid with ink.
Like the shape of an ace card, except that the shape should be to the extent you want to raise the eyelid because people differ in this respect. Some need a portion of the eyelid to be cut according to how much the eyelid relaxes.
And some need less cutting, all of this according to the relaxation of the eyelid. Then make an incision with a scalpel along the two lines I taught you, starting from the larger canal to the smaller canal, and the incision should be near the natural hair, like the thickness of the forceps.
Then insert the needle into one of the corners of the skin and then loosen it all, then stitch the lips together with a needle and thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood and glue what remains of the threads on the eyebrows with some fine things.
You may wish to do this, or not, then the stitches and threads remain for about three or four days, then treat it, and if you want, leave the wound without stitching and treat it with what dries and contracts, because the eyelid rises when the wound is sealed and joined together, and stitching is better.
So this face of the eyelid, I mentioned it by the ancients, except that there is hardship on the patient, and it is from good work and no danger in it, and another face in the eyelid also, which is to learn on the eyelid a shape like the shape of an ace card as we described. Then raise the eyelid with three needles that are separated or grouped in this image:
Then cut what remains of the eyelid with a small pair of scissors in this image, cutting moderately.
If you cannot hold the forceps, and it does not suit you, take a needle in its eye with thread and insert it in the center of the form, and insert another thread near the larger opening and a third thread near the smaller opening, and gather the threads together with your fingers moderately, then raise your hand with them moderately.
And raise the skin attached to it all as we described, then gather the edges of the wound with the stitching and treat it until it heals. If a hot swelling appears at the time of your cutting or incision, soothe that swelling with the use of pitch and similar soothing ointments.
And it may happen to the lower eyelid that its edges turn inward, so what we mentioned regarding cutting, stitching, cauterization with fire and sharp medication should be used in it. Cauterization with fire or sharp medication is more effective and gentler on the patient than cutting and stitching. Cutting and stitching are also more troublesome.
Cauterization with a reed should be done as follows:  Turn the eyelid and make an incision on its inner side as described, then craft two or three thin reeds or twigs whose length matches that of the eyelid and width is less than the width of a scalpel.
And you should sharpen the ends of them on both sides where the threads will cling, then gently gather them over the remaining portion of the eyelid and tightly pull the reeds from both sides, leaving it for days. The stretched skin dies, darkens, and decays.
Until it falls off by itself, if it delays then trim it with pliers and treat it until it heals. If it unites, the eyelid rises and the edges of the eyelid do not turn inward, and this is the shape of the two reeds crafted in this manner and this measure in length and width:.
Chapter Twelve.
On Raising the Ingrown Hairs from the Eye with a Needle.
If a hair or two hairs need to be worked on, take a fine needle and thread it with a fine, smooth silk thread, then gather its ends and tie them in a very small knot. Let the length of the thread be about a cubit.
Then, in the clamps, place another fine thread without knotting it at the end, and tie its ends if you wish. Then place the patient's head on the stone near the sun so that the work is visible because it is delicate work, then insert the needle with the thread into the base of the extra hair.
And insert it into the eyelid with haste until you bring it out above the natural hair, then pull the thread upward to the clamps and insert that hair, whether one or two or three, no more.
Then pull your hand with it until the hair comes out with the clamps in the eyelid along with the natural hair. If you pulled the clamps and the hair did not come out with them, pull the clamps down with the thread that you had placed in them until the clamps exit from the upper hole.
Then you put the hair back in and pull them both. Do this until it rises in the upper hole and you see it with your eye. Then, release the clamps and thread, take them out, and tighten the eyelid and leave it tightened for two or three days until the hair stays in its place and flesh grows on it.
If the hair is short, either add a long hair from the natural hair so that it rises with it, or leave it until it grows longer after a while, then lift it.
Chapter Thirteen.
On the treatment of hairs that occur in the upper eyelid of the eye.
The one who is afflicted by this hair is called an 'arnibiyyah', and these hairs are either natural or acquired. The acquired ones come from the closure of a wound, a cut, or something like that.
The method of treatment in this case is to make an incision in that abscess and separate its lips, making a wick of cotton between them and tying it until it heals. It is not fitting to use things that dry out and constrict in treating it.
If you do that, the lesion will return worse than it was. Instead, use things that soften it like fenugreek and flaxseed steeped in water mixed with a little bit of cumin and cotton wool soaked in diachylon ointment that has been melted with some fat and applied to the wound.
The aim of treatment is to do everything possible to prevent it from closing up in the same way it was originally. This work we mentioned is only a part of repairing the lesion, not restoring the area to its original form.
Chapter Fourteen.
In Treating an Abscess in the Lower Eyelid
This abscess that is from the lower eyelid,  is truly called a "stratum." It can be natural or accidental. The accidental one is from a wound, cut, or prick, and so forth.
The method of treatment in this case is to take a needle with double thread and insert it into the flesh, passing it from the left corner to the right corner until the thread is at both ends of the flesh. Then, you extend the flesh upward with the needle and cut it with a wide scalpel.
If the eyelid returns to its proper shape, then good. Otherwise, take a spatula and place it on the incision site, turning the eyelid over with it. Make two incisions on the inner side of the eyelid, whose ends meet at the corners of the previously cut section, forming a corner. Until they converge, its shape resembles this shape: .
It is the Greek letter lambda, then remove that flesh as much as the sharp side of it is below the eyelid, and then bring together the separated parts with two sutures using wool thread, then treat it with the softening medications and ointment mentioned until it heals.
And if the lip has been slit by a cut or suture or cauterization, then it is necessary to make a simple incision without hair also on what preceded, then separate the lips with a swab as mentioned.
And the statement of the saying in treating the lip if it is from above or below, that work be carried out according to what appears to you of the form of the lip because it can be very different in appearance, and the craftsman devises the way in whatever way he can.
Until the shape returns to its natural form or approaches it, and the same disease directs you to what is suitable for him of work and tool in most cases,.
The fifteenth chapter.
In the adhesion of the eyelid to the conjunctiva or the cornea.
This adhesion may expose many people that the upper eyelid adheres to the white of the eye and prevents it from easy movement and hinders its natural actions, so it is necessary to insert a pointed probe under the eyelid.
And raise it up or extend it with a suture, then cut the adhesion with a delicate scalpel that is not as sharp as the edge of the scalpel but is slightly so as not to disturb the patient during the work and the scalpel escapes and harms the eye with its sharpness, and the cutting is like you are peeling off that adhesion.
And expect until if the eyelid returns to its natural form and the adhesion heals completely, then at that time pour into the eye salt water and wash it with it or instill from the zinc ointment dissolved in water, then separate between the eyelid and the eye with a cotton thread.
And place above the eye a compress soaked in egg white, and after the third day use crushed ointments until it heals.
The sixteenth chapter.
In cutting off the fingernail and trimming the flesh of the nails.
The scirrhus comes in two types, either it is a nervous type which resembles tough, thin peritoneum, or it is a non-nervous type resembling a hardened white moisture; if iron touches it or one attempts to take it with pliers, it will break.
No pliers have been found to be effective in it, and both types begin from the larger opening until it spreads gradually until it covers the viewer and prevents light and eye movement, and the way to work in cutting it is that he places the patient's head in a stone block.
Then he opens his eyes and you raise the eyelid with your hand, then you take a pliers with little bending and stretch it upwards and then you take a needle and insert a horsehair or cow hair into it along with a strong thread and bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the middle of the scirrhus.
And you thread it with the needle and tie the scirrhus with the thread and stretch it upwards and peel off the side of the scirrhus next to the pupil with the hair as if you are spreading it with the hair to the end of it then cut the rest at the root of the opening with a fine scalpel or a small pair of scissors and leave the natural flesh of the opening.
So that it does not expose from its cut a constant flow of tears, and it may be stretched with the pliers alone or with the thread as we mentioned then peel it with the smooth scalpel the tip which this image shows.
And be careful not to touch the cornea with the scalpel so that it causes a break and the pupil becomes inflamed, then after cutting it, put something in the eye from powdered salt or from the black lead and leave it until another day then treat it as necessary until it heals.
If the scirrhus is non-nervous and you could not insert a needle into it nor get pliers to hold onto it, then this type of scirrhus is often treated with medicines and heals as described in the classification; if you want to cut it, open the patient's eye.
Take a scalpel that is fine, smooth, and has a weak edge like this illustration: . And scrape the tip of the bone with it gently. If you see that it crumbles and frays, and only a trace of the scraping remains, then put some salt into your eye from the zanzibar  (black) or red salt or powdered salt, and hold the eye shut for another day.
Then, repeat the scraping until it is all gone except if a hot tumor obstructs you in your eye, then leave it and treat the hot tumor until it heals, then return to scraping it until it heals. As for the fleshy outgrowth of meat...
For if the fleshy outgrowth harms the eye painfully, then ligate that fleshy outgrowth with a suture and cut some of it away, and do not overdo the cutting lest there be a flow of tears, then instill into the eye socket red or zanzibar salt until it heals.
The Seventeenth Chapter.
On cutting away growths and excess meat in the eye.
A red flesh may grow in the eyes of some people, piled upon itself until it covers the vision or approaches it or overflows onto the eyelids and perhaps the eyelids turn outward resembling a blooming carnation.
And the work on it is that the patient places his head in a stone block, then opens his eyes and seizes that entire red flesh with the sutures placed accordingly.
Or grasp it with pliers or a hook, then cut the first flesh first until all of it is removed by cutting and be careful of the eye lest it be harmed during work, and your cutting should be either with the scalpel that we described in scraping the bone tip or with a small pair of scissors. Like those which are used to pick up threads as they appear in the illustration in this book.
And if the cutting is complete and all the redness has gone, fill the eye with finely ground salt or instill a drop of red zizira or similar potent drugs, and put cotton wool dipped in albumen on top of the eye from the outside to prevent hot swelling.
If some redness remains and the blood overpowers you and you fear hot swelling, leave the eye alone and treat it with something that calms the swelling, then return to the operation until it heals. Do the same for any excess flesh that appears in the eye of this type.
Except that you should avoid treating every weak eye, either by natural remedies or surgery with metal instruments, and do not put your hand into anything of these operations until you see that the organ is capable of it.
The Eighteenth Chapter.
On Removing a Foreign Body from the Eye.
The foreign body is red veins that intertwine on the eye, obscuring vision and weakening the eye with the passing days. It is necessary for you first to examine it: if the eye in which the foreign body is located is strong and there is no other illness in it besides the foreign body.
Then the removal is for you to order the patient to put his head in a box, then attach those veins with a single thread or two, depending on your skill, and the threads should be finely flexible like this:
Or two strands interwoven into one body like this:
Then, with a fine pair of scissors, gently pluck those veins until you see the eye has rid itself of them and the blood has subsided. Be careful not to harm the eye with the edges of the scissors. Let your work be during half the day facing the sun.
And be very careful in your work so as not to cut any other veins. When you finish, instill green or red myrrh into the eye so that its sharpness will eat away at any remaining foreign body. If you cannot remove it all in that hour, then compress the eye with something that soothes eye pain.
Leave it for days until the pain subsides and the hot swelling is calmed, then resume work on this same method until the scar of the incision disappears completely.
Leave it [and have the head of the patient on the student's lap, and the other wipe away tears and examine the front and back of the eye]  The principle in working is to open the eye with fixed or triangular openers held by a student.
Fix [it] and have the head of the patient on the student's lap, and the other wipe away tears and examine the front and back of the eye. And you can choose to begin with the forceps from the upper or lower part of the eye, and it is better that two tweezers be placed in the upper cheekbone, one at the end and the other at the beginning.
And hold it between the middle and index fingers, then attach tweezers from below opposite them. Then grasp with your ring and little finger, and remove your hand gently until you see all the blood vessels have risen. Cut from the smallest end using scissors if possible, or a gentle scalpel.
And insert the needle into the opening and straighten all the blood vessels until they rise on the ligament, and do not cut off the weeping for if tears and blood mix you will be in trouble.
Then cut with the scissors all that exceeds the edge from above and below until nothing remains except in the cornea. If you can raise it from the cornea, detach it with the needle; this is better, and it may be difficult for some people.
And if you have cut it, let it remain untouched for days until the pain subsides and the hot swelling calms, then resume working on it.
Chapter Nineteen.
On restoring the feather to the nose.
Physicians call the feather a "nasus" if it is treated with cautery or sharp, corrosive medicine as described above and does not heal, there is no remedy except to open the swelling when ripe and extract all the moisture or pus within it.
Until the bone is revealed, and if the bone is revealed and you see damage or blackness in it, separate it with a tool whose image is:
And it is called the rasp, made from Indian iron, and its head is rounded like a pearl. Fine engravings of the chisel or scalpel are etched on it. You place it on the site of damage in the bone, then turn it between your fingers while you squeeze your hand slightly until you feel that the damage has been separated.
And you do this several times, then cover the site with drying and astringent medicines. If the site is sealed and flesh grows in it, the flow stops and it remains for forty days, not renewing, not being disturbed, and no incident occurring to it.
So know that it has healed, otherwise there is no remedy but to return the  inserted probe to the nasal passage in this manner: reveal the bone again with iron or a sharp medicine. If the bone is revealed, take a swab soaked on this form:.
Its tip is triangular and its shaft is conical, tapering towards the end as you see. Then place it on the bone itself, near the nasal passage and slightly farther away from the eye with your hand, then turn your hand with the swab until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it.
If he feels air coming out of it when he holds his nose, then cover the site with drying and astringent medicines as I have taught you. If flesh grows and the place hardens, the material that was protruding outwards returns to the nose, which is easier for the patient, God willing.
The Twentieth Chapter.
In Returning an Inturned Eye.
If the eye is turned inwards, with no damage or loss to sight, it should be made easier for the patient, then it should be separated in the skull and a small bandage placed on the back of the head without any condition, and a fine syringe used.
Then you place on the eye a poultice made of acacia gum, frankincense, and resin, and then bind the eye from above with a pad using many layers, and the recipe for the layers is to take a soft burning cotton fabric and fold each piece of it four times to make many.
Then you place them one on top of the other as much as the eye needs, and then bind it with a strong, firm piece of cloth, and reapply the dressing from inside without a condition, then remove the dressing and leave the eye bound for a day and night.
If the bandage relaxes during that time, it is necessary to tighten it again, then remove the bandage after a day and night as we said. If you see that the eye has returned, otherwise, reapply the dressing, layers, tightening, and dressing until it returns.
The twenty-first chapter.
In cutting the eyelid.
If a hernia appears in the eyelid layer and it protrudes outside the eyelids like the shape of a fig and disfigures the appearance of the human being, and you want to cut it, then the work is done as I describe.
And it is that you insert a needle into the base of the hernia from below to above, then insert another needle into it with a doubled thread from the side of the mouth, and pass through it and leave the first needle as it is.
Then you cut the place where the doubled thread bends and tie some of the hernia around the needle, tighten it well, then remove the needle and put on the eye cotton soaked in egg white and leave it until the threads fall off with the hernia, then treat the eye with what strengthens it.
Until the wound heals, and you may tighten the eyelid from each side with a circle of cloth until the eye becomes more relaxed, then apply a fine scalpel that reaches the depth of the eye so that the egg white moisture drains and the eye descends and shrinks on its place, then tighten it until it heals.
The Twenty-Second Chapter
On treating the carbuncle.
This ailment called a carbuncle is a swelling that gathers in the eye, resembling water flowing down but not being water, and the way to treat it is to make the patient sit on a straight-backed chair, then take his head in your hands from both sides.
And move him until you see the swelling descend downwards with your eye, then it settles and does not move, and light flows and the patient sees things as he used to, if it doesn't descend downwards we know that it is water, if the swelling doesn't appear to descend as mentioned.
Otherwise, have the patient sit before you and take a fine scalpel and make a small incision above the cornea at the junction of the carbuncle with the cornea in the circle until the matter comes out.
If it comes out, pour into the eye hot water that you have mixed with honey or water that has been boiled with quince seeds and honey, then treat him with the rest of the treatment until he heals.
The Twenty-Third Chapter
We have mentioned the types of water in the classification and which one is suitable for cupping with a detailed and explained explanation, so take it from there on sound health. Then, it becomes necessary to make the patient sit before you comfortably facing the light near the sun.
And tie his healthy eye and pull it tight, then lift the eyelid of his eye with your left hand if the eye that has water is the left eye or with your right hand if it is the right eye.
Then place the tip of the cupping glass near the circle at a thick, strong suction in the white of the eye from the side of the smaller pupil, then push the cupping glass forcefully while turning it with your hand until it penetrates the white of the eye and you feel that the cupping glass has reached something empty.
It is necessary that the depth of the probe's insertion correspond to the distance from the pupil to the end of the blackness, which is the circle of the eye, for the copper is seen by the viewer in the same way as the eye itself because of the transparency of the cornea, then the probe goes above to the place where the water is.
Then you press it down repeatedly, if the water descends from its time, then the patient sees what has been opened to his sight from his time and the probe in his eye, then it settles for a while, if the water rises, bring it down again without removing the probe.
If it settles and does not rise, then remove the probe gently while you slightly wrinkle your hand with it, then dissolve in the water a little bit of pure salt and wash the eye from inside with it, then place over the entire eye from outside a compress or cotton wool soaked in water.
Rub it with rosewater and egg white, and tie the healthy eye to it, but as for us and our people we place cumin powder mixed with egg white on top, if the probe does not enter the eye due to its hardness because there are people whose eyes are very hard indeed. Where you need to take the forceps called the "brid," which has the following image:
Then you drill with it the very place of the adhesion only and do not insist on drilling, but rather you gently direct the probe into a tender spot then insert the probe as we have mentioned, and upon completion of your work prepare for the patient to lie down tightly in a darkened room on his back.
And he refrains from all movements and coughing, and you make his food what softens his nature, and he does not move his head right or left at all, and the bandage remains on him until the third day, then dress his wound in that darkened room and try his sight.
And show him things then return the bandage until the seventh day, and it is not necessary to do that during the time of treatment or after the water rises from its time but rather avoid doing so before the water quickly ascends due to intense looking.
If a hot tumor appears, it is necessary to cauterize the eye before the seventh day and do this with something that calms the tumor until it subsides, then at that time release its vision and place on its face a blindfold which trains its vision from underneath for days while he is in that dark room.
He exits the house gradually and behaves in his affairs, and know that the surgeon cannot dispense with observation many times, then he proceeds to the work, and I have heard from some Iraqis that it has been said that they make a suction cup in Iraq which absorbs water with it.
