Chapter Twenty-Four.
On treating flesh that grows in the nose.
Flesh may grow in the nose of various kinds, some of it like a scorpion with many legs, and some of it is cancerous flesh, hard-colored, and some of it is soft flesh not hard-colored.
And if any of this flesh is soft, it is not malignant nor cancerous, then it is necessary for the patient to sit before you facing the sun and open his nostrils and place the forceps in that flesh and then pull it outwards and cut what you grasped from it with a sharp fine scalpel from one side.
Until you know that all the flesh has gone, and if something remains of it which you could not cut, remove it with one of the gentle instruments gently so that nothing remains of it, then if blood overpowers you or a hot tumor appears.
Then meet it with what is necessary, or if it was from the malignant tumors, then hasten to cauterize it until the bleeding stops and all the flesh goes away, and after cutting, place water or a drink in the nose so that the nostrils open and moisture flows down into the throat.
Know that if he has healed, and if the moisture has not run off as it should, know that his inside is meat raw in the upper part of the loose bone;  the instrument did not reach it with a cut, so then you must take a thread from linen which has some thickness.
And you knot it with many knots and make between each knot the measure of a finger or less, and the patient moves his hand to insert one end of the thread into his nose with moderation or whatever he is able, after making it like a bead, and you pull on its wind until it reaches the nostril.
And it comes out on his throat, and many times the boys do such an act in schools, which is easy for whoever wants to do it, then you bring together the two ends of the thread, one that came out on the mouth and the other that remained in the nose.
Then you use the spreading of flesh with the knots in the thread, doing so until you learn that the flesh has been cut by the thread of the knot, then you take out the thread and it remains in the nose after wiping the blood, a wick which has soaked in Egyptian ointment, do this for three days or more.
Until the ointment eats up all that remains of the flesh, then the last thing in the nose becomes a lead pipe for days until it heals, if he needs treatment to dry it out, you used that.
And this is a picture of the spout which drips medicines into the nose:
It is placed from silver or copper like a small candlestick, open on the inside and with a channel as well.
And if you wish, you make the tube closed like a pipe and the spout of the ointment flat.
It has a handle at its end, as you see, and you grasp it when the fat is heated in it or whatever from juices or things that are fluid.
The twenty-fifth chapter.
In cases of nasal polyps growing at the tip of the nose.
Often, a polyp grows at the tip of the nose and increases in size with the days until it becomes unsightly.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut it at its first appearance and remove all of it. Then apply to the place either a cautery or a burning medicine that replaces the cautery. If cutting it is delayed until it grows large, look if it is hard and rigid like wood with little sensation.
Do not expose it to iron, for it is a cancerous tumor and I have often seen that from cutting this tumor a great affliction returned upon its owner. If the tumor is soft to the touch and not rigid in color, and you see that cutting can be done throughout it all. Then, empty the ailment and cut it without hesitation or stopping, and treat the place with what dries and contracts until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-Sixth.
On stitching up the nose, lip, and ear. If the connection of them is severed from a wound or similar, know that when the connection is severed in one of these cartilages, little that is helpful can be done except for some people.
Therefore, when one is presented with something like that, look if the wound is fresh with blood, then gather the edges of the wound with stitching and treat it until it heals. If the separation of the connection has separated its edges and each incision became whole, then it is necessary to scarify each incision with the thickness of its visible skin until it bleeds.
Then, gather the edges with stitching and tighten them, and apply a poultice of frankincense and mastic powder on top. Place from above the gauze a plaster of palm ointment or another binding ointment and leave it tightened for two or three days then unwrap it.
The drug is changed and left until the threads separate themselves, then it is treated with ointment until it heals. The description of suturing is to bring together the separated parts, either with needles as we described in the stitching of the abdomen, or with thread as we have informed you there.
The twenty-seventh chapter.
On extracting a knot that has appeared in the lips.
Many people may appear to have small, hard tumors inside their lips, some resembling a corn, and others smaller or larger. Therefore, it is necessary to turn the lip and cut on each knot, and attach it with a suture.
And it is cut from each side, then the place after cutting is stuffed with powdered alum until the bleeding stops, and it is rinsed with vinegar, salt, and the places are treated with what is inside them until the wounds heal.
The twenty-eighth chapter.
On cutting excess flesh in the gums.
Often, excess flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call apulus. Therefore, it should be sutured or grasped with a forceps, and cut at its root, and the time is left to drain or bleed, then powdered alum is placed on the site.
Or one of the clamping, drying points if that flesh returns after treatment, it often returns so cut it again and cauterize it, for it does not return after cauterization.
The twenty-ninth chapter.
On extracting teeth with iron.
Sometimes, coarse, unsightly scales may gather on the surfaces of teeth from inside and outside, and between the gums. They may darken, yellow, and turn green until this causes decay to reach the gums, and disfigures the teeth for that reason.
Therefore, it is necessary to make the patient sit between your hands and their head on a stone, and extract the molar and tooth where you see scales and something like sand until nothing remains of it, and do the same with the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and so on until it is cleansed.
If what is in it from the first stage of the extraction goes, otherwise you return to it with the forceps another day and a second and a third until you reach the goal of what you want, know that the molar requires different shapes and many forms of forceps according to what is suitable for your work.
For the forceps that extracts a tooth from inside is not like the one that extracts it from outside, and the one that extracts it between teeth is in another form, and these are several forms of forceps that you have all prepared.
Chapter Thirty.
On Tooth Extraction.
It is necessary to treat the molar for its pain with all means and delay its extraction, as there is no substitute for it if it is extracted because it is a noble essence, even if there is no other choice but to extract it.
And when the patient decides to extract it, it is necessary to ensure that the painful molar tooth is sound for you. For often the patient deceives himself about the pain and thinks it is in the sound tooth, so he extracts it, then the pain does not go away until he extracts the diseased molar, we have seen this many times from the actions of barbers.
If the painful molar tooth is sound for you, then it is necessary to circumcise around the tooth with a scalpel that has some strength until the gums are separated from all sides, then move it with your fingers or with the delicate forceps first a little at a time until you dislodge it.
Then, you can then seize it with the two large forceps with a firm grip and the patient's head between your knees held securely so that he does not move, then pull the tooth straight so as not to break it. If it does not come out, otherwise take one of those instruments and insert it under it from each side gently and shake it as you did at first.
If the molar tooth is perforated or fractured, it is necessary to fill that hole with a piece of felt and plug it tightly with a fine point so that it does not come loose while you are pulling on it with pliers, and it is necessary to investigate by probing around the gum from all sides indeed.
And be cautious in your effort so that you do not break it, for if some remains it will return on the sick person as a pain greater than his first pain, and avoid doing what ignorant blacksmiths do in their bridge and rushing to demolish without using what we have described.
For often they inflict great harm on people, the least of which is that the molar tooth breaks and its roots remain, all or some. Or that they may extract some of the jawbone as we have seen many times, then gargle after its extraction with wine or vinegar and salt, if bleeding occurs from the place, then often it happens so tamp it at that time with a little bit of saffron and fill the place.
Or if that does not work for you, we have the image of the pliers, the delicate ones by which the molar is moved first, its ends should be long and the handle short and thick so that it does not bend when you grasp it with the molar, and this is the image of the large pliers:.
They are as you see, thick handles so that when you grasp them they do not give themselves and do not bend, short ends, and let them be of Indian steel or well-forged hardened steel with tips that enter each other so that it grips tightly and securely.
And you can make the ends like a chisel, they will also be strong in clamping.
Chapter Thirty-Three.
In Extracting the Roots of Teeth and Removing Broken Jawbones.
If the root of a tooth remains after its extraction, and is broken, it is necessary to place cotton soaked in oil on the site for a day or two until the site relaxes, then insert the forceps or tweezers into it. Which resemble its edges the beak of the bird called the bulbul, and this is a picture of the tweezers: .
It is made like a scalpel from inside or like an eskefal. If it does not work for you to remove it with these tweezers, then it is necessary to dig on the root and expose all the flesh with the scalpel, then insert the tool that resembles a small pulley, and this is its picture:.
Short at the end, slightly thick and not smooth so that it does not break. If the root comes out with this, otherwise use these other tools, and this is their picture, the first one is three-pointed at the end with some thickness: .
A picture of another delicate threefold :.
And we can also use this tool with two prongs, and this is its picture too: .
And with other tools and instruments mentioned in the record of teeth, we can also use this tool that resembles a large spindle, and this is its picture: .
Three-pointed at the end, curved and slightly thick so that it does not break, and not smooth. Know that tools for teeth are many, as well as all other instruments, they are hardly countable, and the skilled craftsman in his craft may invent tools for himself according to what the work and diseases themselves indicate.
Because some diseases have not been mentioned for which the ancients created tools due to their different types, if a bone from the jaw or one of the bones of the mouth breaks or decays, search for it in its place with what suits him from one of these tools and tweezers that were mentioned in extracting the roots.
And we use forceps, and this is its picture: .
There should be some thickness, a little bit, to control the bone so that it does not slip until the bone is brought out, and we compress the place with medicines suitable for this purpose. If the bone has slight decay, remove its decay and blackness until it is purified, then treat it until it heals.
Chapter Thirty-Two.
In the emergence of teeth growing on others.
If teeth emerge on a path other than their natural course, they become misshapen, especially if this happens in women and slaves. It is necessary to look, and if the tooth has emerged behind another tooth.
And if it could not be moved or pushed back, then remove it. And if it is attached to another tooth, cut it with this instrument whose image is:
And it resembles a small beak, and let it be from Indian steel, very sharp at the tip, and your cutting should be done for many days due to the hardness of the tooth so that you do not disturb the other teeth. As for if it emerged firmly rooted, then push it back with a cold chisel whose image is:
It should all be from India and its end be very finely engraved, resembling the chisel used for making needles. Use it to gently push back the tooth a little at a time over many days so that you do not shake the tooth and make it fall out, then file it afterwards and remove it with some pliers.
And if a tooth has broken off from it, and it hurts the tongue when speaking, then it is necessary to also push it back until the roughness of that breakage goes away and it becomes level and smooth so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt speech.
Chapter Thirty-Three.
In bracing the loose teeth with silver wires or gold wires.
If the front teeth become loose and move from a blow or fall, and the patient cannot bite on anything to eat lest they fall out, and you treated them with astringent medicines, but the treatment was ineffective.
The remedy for this is to sew it with a gold or silver thread, and gold is better because silver rusts and decays after days, and gold remains in its state forever, it does not undergo that, and the thread should be medium in thickness and width according to what can fit between the teeth.
And the way to weave it is to take the thread and put its loop between the two healthy teeth, then weave at both ends of the thread between the mobile teeth, one or more, until the weaving reaches the healthy tooth from the other side.
Then she re-weaves to the side where it began and pulls her hand gently and wisely so that it does not move at all, and the tightening of the thread is at the roots of the teeth so that it does not slip, then she cuts the ends of the excess thread with the scissors and gathers them together and weaves them into a knot with the pliers and hides them between the healthy tooth and the mobile tooth.
So that it does not harm the tongue, then she leaves it like this tightened for as long as it remains. If it unravels or its tightness breaks, she tightens it with another thread, and she enjoys it like this throughout her life, and this is the image of the teeth and the appearance of weaving in two healthy teeth and two mobile teeth as you see:
And the fallen tooth or two may be returned to its place and woven as we described, and it remains. But this is done by a skilled craftsman, and he may carve bone from the bones of a cow to make it in the shape of a tooth and put it in the place where the tooth fell out. And he tightens it as we said, and it remains, and he enjoys that.
Chapter Forty-Third.
On cutting the tether under the tongue that prevents speech.
This tether under the tongue may be natural, which a human is born with, or it may be accidental from an injury that has healed.
The procedure is to open the patient's mouth and head in a stone, raise their tongue, then cut that nerve ligament across until the tongue releases from its hold. If there is some stiffness and complexity because of an old wound, insert a suture into it and cut it across until the ligament breaks and the knot dissolves.
Beware that the cut not be in the depth of the flesh so that a vein is cut there and bleeding occurs. Then, rinse the area after the cutting with rose water or vinegar and cold water, then put under the tongue a cotton wick which the patient holds every night.
So that it doesn't fuse again, if bleeding occurs, put powdered saffron on the spot, and if the blood overcomes you, cauterize the place with a convex lens burner suitable for that purpose. Then treat it with all other treatments until it heals.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
On extracting the frog born under the tongue.
A growth under the tongue may occur resembling a small frog, preventing the tongue from its natural function and perhaps growing until it fills the mouth. The procedure is to open the patient's mouth facing the sun and look at the growth.
If you see it black in color or hard, with no sensation for the patient, do not touch it, as it is cancer. If it leans towards whiteness and has moisture, suture into it and cut it with a delicate scalpel and remove it from every side.
If you are overcome with blood while working, put powdered saffron on it until the bleeding stops, then return to your work until you remove it completely, and then rinse with vinegar and salt.
Then treat it with all other appropriate treatments until it heals.
Chapter Thirty-Six.
In the Treatment of Tonsil Tumors
And what grows in the throat from other tumors, may appear inside the throat glands that resemble the glands that appear externally and are called tonsils; if treated with what has been mentioned in the classification and it did not heal.
Look then, if the tumor is hard like lead and has little feeling, do not expose it to iron. And if it is red in color and its base is thick, do not also expose it to iron for fear of bleeding, but leave it until it ripens; either it will subside by itself or it will burst from itself.
And if it is white in color and round, and its base is soft, this is what should be cut. And the work done in it is that you look before you work, whether the heat of the tumor has subsided completely or some lessening.
So, when this is the case, seat the patient with his feet in the sun and his head on a stone and open his mouth and take an assistant by your hand who presses his tongue down with a tool whose image is:
It is made of silver or copper and is thin like a knife. When you press the tongue down with it, the tumor becomes visible to you; then take pliers and insert them into the tonsil, and pull it outwards as much as possible without pulling anything from the peritoneum along with it.
Then cut it with a tool whose image is like scissors, but the ends of each are turned so that each end is very sharp towards the other; it is made of Indian iron or Damascus steel:
If this tool is not available, then cut it with a scalpel whose image is:
Sharp on one side and not sharp on the other side, so after cutting one tonsil you cut the other in the same manner of cutting, then after the cutting, gargle the patient with cold water or vinegar and water.
If he has bleeding that is gaping, apply water mixed with the rind of pomegranates or fig leaves or something similar until the bleeding stops, then treat it until it heals. And sometimes growths may appear in the throat other than the tonsils, so they are removed as described for removing tonsils.
I treated a woman who had a tumor that had grown inside her throat, pressing against the esophagus, with little feeling, almost closing the throat. The woman was breathing through a narrow passage and it prevented her from eating or drinking water.
And she was close to death if she had lived for another day or two, and the tumor grew from it two branches until they came out of her nostrils. So I acted quickly, I inserted a hook into one of them and pulled it, and a piece that was healthy came out.
Then I cut it where I reached it from the nostril, and I did the same with what protruded from the other nostril, then I opened her mouth and pressed her tongue down, and inserted the hook into the tumor itself, then cut some of it, and only a little blood came out.
Then the woman's throat opened, and she immediately began to drink water, then she was able to eat, and we continued to cut from that tumor repeatedly for a long time, and the tumor would grow back in place of what we cut until it took a long time for both of us.
Then her throat healed, and the tumor inside her throat disappeared so it stopped growing, then she traveled from that place and I did not know what God had done to her after me.
Chapter thirty-seven.
On removing a tumor of the palate.
The one called a  â€˜plumâ€™ if it descended from the throat to the palate and swelled up and was white and oblong, then it is called â€˜a columnâ€™. And if it was thick at the bottom and round, then it is called a plum. If it was treated with what we mentioned in the classification, and the treatment did not work.
I saw the hot swelling had subsided and it was delicate, so it should be cut. And that which of it was not joined together in a round shape and did not have length and was either bloody or like the color of bile or black or without feeling, it is necessary to avoid cutting it.
There is danger for the sick person in this, so it is necessary when you see it on the description that was mentioned of its whiteness and length, that you make the sick person sit facing the sun and press his tongue with the instrument which is described before, then insert the probe into the cavity.
And pull it down and cut it with one of the two instruments which were mentioned in cutting the tonsils, and it is necessary that you do not cut from it except what increased beyond the natural order without addition because if you cut more from it, you will harm the voice and speech.
Then after the cutting, you use what we described in cutting the tonsils and treat it until it heals, if the sick person refuses to have it cut, it is necessary that you use the trick in its treatment without fear or caution, and the appearance of the treatment is with the sharp medicine which is to put the head of the sick person in a stone.
Then you press his tongue with the instrument which we mentioned, then take from the sharp water that was mentioned in the chapter on treatment and knead with it a dough not extinguished, making it neither thick nor thin, and fill this instrument with it and this is its form:
Its end which you put in the medicine is a cavity like the cavity of a moroccan spoon, and you put the instrument with the medicine on the same place and the sick person lying on his side so that saliva flows from within his throat so that nothing will go down into his throat to harm him.
Then you hold your hand with the medicine and squeeze it on the place for half an hour until you see that it has turned black and the sting of the medicine subsided, if you want to take cotton, wrap it around the end of a moroccan spoon and dip the cotton in the medicine.
Insert cotton into a tube from above until the cotton adheres to the surface. Do this repeatedly until you reach the desired thickness of the plug, then leave it. It will dry and fall off after three or four days. If you need to reapply the medicine, repeat the process.
After the plug is in place, wipe around the wound with cotton soaked in butter and use it to remove any medicine that has spread. Then rinse with cold water and treat externally with poultices and internally with gargles until healed. This type of treatment is safer than cutting and less frightening.
The wound can also be treated with something milder than a plug or cutting. It is treated with incense in this way: take saffron, wormwood, spurge, henbane, frankincense, hyssop, and similar herbs. Gather all of them, or some of them, in a pot and immerse them in vinegar.
Bring to a boil with the pot covered in clay from the wise man's workshop. Make a hole in the center of the lid and place the perforated instrument on it, which is made of silver or copper:
Insert the end with the sieve into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the wound through the tube, so that the wound is properly covered. Repeat this several times until it dries out. Beware of doing this treatment at the first occurrence of the tumor.
Because it often increases the tumor, it is best to do this when the tumor has subsided and become less hot. If you don't have this instrument, take a tube and attach an eggshell to its end so that the patient's mouth doesn't burn.
Because the eggshell prevents the heat of the vapor from burning the mouth, and this is a good treatment with safety.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
On extracting thorns and other things that lodge in the throat.
Often a bone, or thorn of fish or something similar lodges in the throat and it is necessary to remove what is visible to the eye after compressing the tongue with the instrument at the sun.
So that what is in the throat may become clear to you, and if it does not appear and remains hidden in the throat, it is necessary to induce vomiting in the patient before he swallows his food into his stomach, for perhaps the lodged thing will be brought up by vomit, or the patient will swallow a piece of bread or the root of a leek.
or he may swallow a mouthful of dry bread or take a piece of soft sea sponge, tie it to a thread, and have him swallow it, then when it reaches the place of the thorn, pull on the thread quickly, do this several times.
For often the thorn or bone gets stuck there and comes out, but if it does not come out by what has been mentioned, then use an instrument of lead in this form:
It should be a little thicker than the reed, and at its end there is a groove into which the patient inserts in his throat gently while raising his head upwards, taking care not to touch his larynx so that he may not cough, and push out the bone or thorn, or the physician himself may insert it with his hand.
And it is better for the patient to insert it, as he knows the place of the lodged thing and pushes downwards or pulls his hand with the instrument upwards, all this according to what seems best for him until it comes out.
The Ninth Thirty-First Chapter.
In Removing Lodged Things from the Throat.
If you have treated the lump with what was mentioned in the division of treatment by medicines and it did not benefit, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun after compressing his tongue with the instrument that has been described to you.
If your sight falls upon the lump, draw it out with a small snare or a soft and firm thread; if you cannot do so with this, then take a hollow tube, insert it into the throat of the patient near the lump, then insert a piece of iron heated in fire into the inside of the tube.
Do this several times and the patient abstains from water all day, then he takes a mouthful of cold water and opens his mouth in it and gargles with it and does not swallow even a drop, and moves the water sometimes with his hand.
For if the phlegm falls on the place when it feels water, and if it does not come out as we described, then gargle the throat with urine and the solution with the instrument that was described in the incense of the throat several times for it will fall.
And the way to work with the incense is to take a pot containing hot coals from the fire and the pot covered with a lid in its center a hole, then insert the tip of the instrument into that hole, then throw the incense and the patient puts his mouth at the end of the tube and closes his mouth so that the incense does not come out until he feels that the incense has reached his throat.
For if the phlegm falls on the place, and if it does not fall, then the incense is repeated several times, and the patient endures thirst and eats salt and garlic and does not drink water, there is no doubt that it will come out with this method, and this is a picture of an instrument used to draw out phlegm from the throat when it comes into view.
And it resembles the tweezers as you see, except that it has this attachment that enters the throat and its ends resemble the beak of a bird; there is roughness in the cold iron if it pressed on something, it would not leave it.
And another instrument that presses on the tongue, it is a wide ring of iron the size of the mouth, above the tongue, it enters the mouth standing on its side, and the mouth remains open without the patient's will, and he cannot remove it at all until it is moved.
The description of the instrument that opens the mouth in this exact way.
Chapter Forty.
Here we discuss the discourse on tumors and their incision.
Tumors have many diverse types, as will be mentioned individually in this book, and they differ in their treatment and incision from two aspects: one is the nature of the tumor itself and what it contains of fluids.
The second aspect is from the location where they occur in the body, because a tumor that occurs in the head is not like a tumor that occurs in the buttock, and a tumor that occurs in a place of fleshy tissue is not like a tumor that occurs in a joint; each one has its own ruling on how to treat it.
And some tumors should not be incised except after the pus within them has ripened and matured, and some should be incised while they are immature and have not fully ripened, such as tumors that are close to the joints.
Because if a tumor occurs near a joint and its duration is prolonged until it decays around it, it may damage the ligaments or nerves of that joint, which could cause paralysis of that limb or because the tumor is near a major organ.
Because if you delay its incision until it matures, you will harm that major organ or because it is near the buttock, you should incise it while immature; however, it is obligatory to excise an immature tumor near the buttocks so that it does not decay and penetrate into the buttock, making it a fistula.
And it becomes in a way that does not heal, and it is necessary to know the time of incision for tumors that have fully ripened, which is when the pain of the tumor subsides, fever disappears, redness and swelling decrease, the head of the tumor softens, and all other signs.
And it is necessary to make the incision at the bottom of the tumor's location if possible, so that it is easier for the fluid to drain downwards or in the softest place of the tumor and most protruding, and let the incision be lengthwise along the body if the tumors are in the hands or feet.
And locations of the muscles and tendons and nerves and arteries, and in general all flat places without bending, but as for the places that bend, it should go with a knife according to that place. And if the swelling is in fleshy places, it is best to leave its incision.
Until it ripens as we said completely, if you cut into it before that, the pus will flow from it for a long time and be much harmful and dirty, and perhaps its lips will harden and its depths will become obstructed, and some tumors can be incised on the side of the body when necessary or according to what the limb needs.
In small tumors, one incision should be used, and in large tumors, a wide incision or many incisions according to the size of the tumor. And some tumors may need to have the skin pulled tight and cut if it has become like parchment.
And it may become to some extent dead like what is found in many blisters and abscesses, and some of them are cut with a three-cornered incision, and some are cut from it in the shape of an Arabic fig leaf.
And some of them use the round incision and the crescent-shaped incision and similar incisions, and if it does not have a head like smooth, flat tumors, it is necessary to cut it with a simple incision only. And it should be done when the tumor is large and has gathered for a long time and it has been cut into, do not rush to remove all the pus at that time.
Rather, extract some of it, then tighten the tumor for another day and then extract some more pus, do this repeatedly in stages until all of it is removed.
Especially if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or a young child, or an elderly man, because the animal spirit often dissolves with the expulsion of pus in one go, and perhaps the patient will die while you do not feel it. So beware of this matter with great caution.
After striking these tumors it is necessary to cleanse the wound and look. If the tumor's wound is small or the incision one simple one, use a gauze of cotton or lint. If the tumor is large and the incisions many.
It is necessary to introduce into each incision a thread until some of them reach each other. If the tumor has been cut from the skin some of it or hardened, it is necessary to pack it with lint or hemp cotton without dampness and tighten it until the third day.
Then remove it and treat it with what is necessary of ointments until it heals. If bleeding occurs during the work, use cold water and vinegar after soaking a cotton cloth in them and apply it to the place of bleeding several times.
If the bleeding persists, it is necessary to use the measures, treatment and dressings that we have described in many places in this book of ours and the classification. If you are in wintertime and the place of the tumor is rich in nerves, it is necessary to wet the pads with a hot drink and oil.
And place them on the place. If you are in summer and the places are fleshy, it is necessary to carry the pads soaked with water and oil or with a drink and oil all of that cold until if it is the third day as we have said, it is necessary to remove the tumor and cleanse it.
And use in its treatment what is similar to it until it heals. This is what you need to know about the treatment of tumors in general. As for the way of detail, I have mentioned each tumor how the way to treat it is summarized and classified.
Chapter Forty-one.
In the incision on tumors that appear in the skin of the head.
Tumors small in size appear in the skin of the head and are of the type of cysts containing them that have conditions such as a hen's egg sac and their types are numerous, some fatty, others containing moisture resembling mud.
Some of them contain moisture resembling broth and soup, and some are hard and solid, all of which pose no danger when cut and removed unless you encounter a vein when cutting into them.
And the work in cutting into them is to first soften them with the instrument whose image comes after this one which is called the "madass" until you learn what they contain. If what they contain is moisture, then cut it lengthwise with a simple incision as shown in this image: .
And begin the incision from line ~b~ to line ~j~.  If the moisture is drained, then peel off the sac that contained that moisture and cut it all up, leaving nothing of it at all, because it often returns if something remains of it.
Then, dip cotton in the salve if it is available; otherwise, in salt water, and fill the wound with it and leave it until the next day, because it eats what remains of the sac. Then, apply the cotton dipped in the salve again and a third time if needed.
Until you are certain that nothing of the sac remains. Then, treat the wound with salves until it heals. And if the swelling contains a fatty mass, cut into it as shown in this image:.
A longitudinal incision and the scalpel at the edge of the wound, peel it from each side, and exert effort in removing the peritoneum that contains it. If you encounter a vein, do what I have described to you before, and do the same with the swelling if it is hardened upon cutting.
And the treatment in this case is as I have mentioned, and the incision on the hardened swelling is easier because it contains little blood and moisture. And perhaps some of these swellings in the head in some people contain no moisture at all, for example when I cut into a swelling...
The head of an old woman, I found the swelling like a solid stone, rough and white, that could not be broken by anyone, even if someone threw it, and none of the other swellings that occur in the head were like this except for those that appear on the heads of children.
When you reach the root of the ear, make a simple incision all around it and make its bottom to be from its lower part so that the flow of material is easier downward, then treat it with what suits it of treatment.
The Twenty-fourth Chapter.
In the incision on the tumors that appear in the neck, these tumors often appear in the neck and under the armpits and in the groin; they can appear all over the body. The one that appears in the neck is sometimes single and sometimes multiple, and some are generated from others.
And every tumor among them is within a special peritoneum, just as in the tumors of the head and the hernia, as we described; and there are many kinds of these tumors, some petrified, some containing moisture, and some malignant that do not respond to treatment.
So I did not see any of them in good health when touched, and its appearance was close to the color of the skin, it moved in every direction, and it was not attached to a nerve in the neck or to a tendon or a vein, nor was it sunken. Where it is necessary to make an incision in it, a simple incision from above to the bottom of the body, along this line from line ~g~ to line ~b~.
And peel it from every side and stretch the edges of the skin with a ligature or two ligatures, or many ligatures if necessary, as we said in the tumors of the head, and take it out little by little, being careful that it does not cut a vein or nerve, and let the scalpel be not too sharp.
So that your hand does not increase the cutting or disturb the patient, cut what you do not need to cut; if you cut a vein or artery and it prevents you from working, put powdered alum or some of the things that stop bleeding in the wound.
And tighten the wound and leave it until the intensity of the tumor subsides and the wound relaxes and begins to heal; for the blood flow stops then, return to your work until you finish, then examine with your index finger if there are any other small tumors remaining, cut them and clean them.
If there is a large vein in the root of the pig, it is necessary not to cut the pig from its root but rather to tie it with a double and tight thread and leave it until it falls off by itself without harm. Then the wound is stuffed with cotton wool that has been soaked in Egyptian ointment and then treated.
And if the pig is cut entirely, it is necessary to bring the edges of the wound together and sew it from its hour after you have learned that there is no leftover piece of the pig. If you see that there is some leftover because of the size of the pig.
If it is necessary to aim at its root and base with the cutting and use the suture mentioned, and if any of the pigs contain moisture, line them with a simple pad where you see the place of ripeness and make the pad as follows below as we said.
Then use after the pad, lint with Egyptian ointment and the like to eat what remains of the rot until when you see that the wound has healed, treat it with ointments for the flesh until it is healed.
The thirty-fourth chapter.
In a slit in the larynx about a tumor that occurs inside the throat.
The ancients mentioned this slit in the larynx, and I have not seen anyone in our country make it. This is their way of speaking. As for those who suffer from angina, they should avoid cutting the larynx because they do not benefit from it.
Because all the ailments and lungs are weak, and as for those who have a hot tumor in the mouth or throat or tonsils if there is no cause in the windpipe, it is necessary to use a slit in the larynx to escape from the defect that arises from suffocation.
It is necessary, if we desire this, to cut the larynx under three circles of the trachea or four small cuts lengthwise between two circles as much as the cut in the peritoneum and not in cartilage. This position agrees with the cut.
Since it is devoid of flesh and blood vessels are distant from it, if the surgeon is cowardly he should stretch the skin of the throat with a ligature then split the skin until reaching the trachea he should avoid blood vessels if he sees any.
Then he should split the peritoneum which we described, and deduce the trachea's incision from the phlegm that exits with it along with the shortness of breath and the stopping of the voice, and leave the wound open for a time. When the time passes in which there was fear of suffocation, bring together the edges of the wound from the skin.
And its plan alone without cartilage, then use the medicines that grow flesh until it heals. Said the author of this book, an explanation of this phrase which we have recounted is if they see the patient's throat blocked by one of these tumors they mentioned.
And the patient on the brink of death, his hope dwindling, they went to split the larynx so that the patient could breathe some air on the wound and escape death.  But they were ordered to leave the wound open until the end of the illness and its duration was three days or thereabouts.
Then they ordered the wound to be stitched and treated until it healed. And what I saw with my own eyes, a servant took a knife and sent it on her throat, cutting some of the windpipe with it.  She was called for treatment and found to be wheezing as a slaughtered animal does, so they uncovered the wound.
And I found the blood that came out of the wound to be slow, so I was certain she had not cut an artery or vein.  And air was coming out of the wound. She was treated, and the wound was stitched and treated until it healed. And nothing happened to the servant except a change in her voice, nothing more.
And she returned after days to her best condition. From here we say that splitting the larynx is not dangerous.
The Forty-fourth Chapter.
In the incision on the swelling that appears in the pharynx from outside and is called a pharyngeal fistula.
This swelling that is called a pharyngeal fistula is a large swelling the color of the body and in women it is frequent and it comes in two types.
Either it is natural or acquired, but the natural one there is no treatment for it and as for the acquired one, it comes in two types, one similar to fatty tumors and the other similar to a tumor that arises from the complication of the vein and in its incision there is danger. So it should not be touched with iron at all except for the small ones, if you probe and examine it with a probe, if its appearance is like a fatty tumor and it was not attached to any of the veins, then cut it as you would cut a fatty tumor. And take out what it contains from the sac if it is in a sac, otherwise, investigate all of it then treat the place with the proper treatment.
The Forty-fifth Chapter.
In the incision on types of tumors.
Tumors come in many types and all their types have been mentioned in the classification, but it is necessary to tell here the difference between a tumor and an abscess because it is problematic. I say that an abscess comes with heat, fever, and frightening pain until the boiling of the vein subsides. And the pus completes, then the fever and severity subside, and the tumor does not come with heat, fever, or pain, and it is contained in a sac that is its special container and it is on the color of the body and its beginning is like the lentil and it becomes like the pumpkin, larger and smaller.
And it is of two types, either fatty or that it contains moisture, and the colors of moisture are many as mentioned in the classification, so if you come to treat the tumor, first probe and examine it with the instrument called the probe, as its image will come in the chapter after this.
Measure the size of the swelling, then remove the probe and look at what comes out after it. If a wet fluid of any color comes out, make a simple incision as I mentioned for all swellings.  If no wet fluid comes out after the probe, know that it is fatty.
Make a crosswise incision on it as I taught you, as in this image.  Suspend it with pins and carefully peel the skin from each side, taking care to remove the sac if you can get it out whole with its contents.
If the sac ruptures during the operation and you cannot remove it whole, as this often happens,  remove it in pieces until nothing remains of it, because if anything is left, whether little or much, the contents will most often return.
If you are overpowered and a little remains, scrape the wound at the end of your work with some sharp pointed instruments and tighten the wound. Place something on top that will soothe the hot swelling and treat it with all other treatments until it heals. If the contents were large, outline its edges and treat it with something that will promote healing.
If a strong or weak sweat vein or something else crosses you and causes bleeding, immediately scrape the area with powdered antimony and leave it tight for two or three days until the wound dries and the bleeding subsides, then return to cutting what remains of the contents.

On Images of Instruments

Chapter Forty-Nine.
On cutting warts that appear in the abdomen.
Many people often have warts on their abdomens and other parts of their bodies, called "natural" warts because they resemble fungi. Their base is thin and their head is thick, their edges may be turned in and some are small while others become very large.

The procedure for cutting them is to examine if the patient is wet and if the wart is white, moist, and thin at its base, then cut it with a wide knife and have moxies in fire because often when they are cut, a lot of blood rushes out.

Every time it affects the wart until it detaches and falls off by itself without pain, if the wart has a thick base, then cutting it is somewhat frightening and dangerous, especially if it is in the abdomen, but some of it can be cut or half of it.
Then cauterize it so that it doesn't return, and treat it until the wound heals. Be careful not to cut a wart that is dark in color, has little sensation, and looks rough because it is cancerous, and I will mention cancer after this.
The Twenty-Fifth Chapter.
On the Treatment of Carbuncles.
A carbuncle arises from many causes, either from a rupture in the peritoneum of the abdomen through which pus or intestines come out, as is described in other ruptures, or from blood emanating from a vein or artery as mentioned before, or from trapped air inside it.
If it arises from a rupture in the peritoneum and the protrusion of pus, then the color of the tumor is similar to the color of the body, it is soft without pain and appears in different positions. If it arises from the protrusion of intestines, then its condition is even more different than what we have described. If you press it with your fingers it disappears then returns and perhaps there is a crackling sound, and it increases greatly upon entering the bath or strenuous exertion. If it arises from humidity, then it is soft.
It does not disappear if you press it with your hand, nor does it increase or decrease. If it arises from blood, then along with these signs, the tumor appears to be black. If it arises from a growing lump of flesh, then the tumor is hard and firm and remains at one level.
If it arises from air, upon touching it is soft. The action in this case is to look. If the carbuncle arises from blood of an artery or vein or air, then it is necessary to refrain from treating it because there is fear and danger as I informed you in the chapter where I described tumors that occur due to arteries and veins.
If the carbuncle arises from intestines or pus, then it is necessary to order the sick person to hold himself and stand upright stretched, then draw around the entire carbuncle with a lead pencil. Then order him to lie down in front of you on his back, then cut around the carbuncle with a broad scalpel at the place you drew with the pencil. Then stretch the center of the tumor upwards with a large thread and tie the place of the incision with strong twine or silk thread tightly.
The knot of the bandage is then made, and the middle of the tumor that has been tightened above the bandage is opened. You insert your index finger into it and feel for the intestines. If you find that the bandage has taken them, loosen the knot and push the intestines back into the abdomen. If you find a hernia, pull it in with a string.
And cut its excess, and if a vein or artery obstructs you, tie it securely and return to your work. Then take two needles and insert two strong threads into them. Insert the two needles into the incision you made around the tumor, and cross them, then tighten the tumor in four places on the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and leave the place until the tightened flesh rots and falls by itself or cut it if it softens and rots. Then treat it with what is appropriate of ointments until it heals. If the growth is from flesh that has sprouted in it.
Or if it is from moisture, it is necessary to cut the tumor as we mentioned and remove the blood or moisture you find in it. Then treat it with what heals the place.
