Chapter Eighty-Seven.
On the expulsion of the placenta.
If the placenta is retained after delivery, it is necessary to order the woman to hold herself and then to have her sneeze with a khandus (a type of medicinal snuff), and to grip her hand on her mouth and nostrils. If it comes out by this means, otherwise, take a gourd.
And pierce a hole in the lid and put inside it herbs that open the mouth of the uterus like fudung, sabath, dill, chamomile, shih, salicylic acid, and centaury; all these medicines or some of them. Soak them in water and place them on the fire, then put a silver tube on the hole of the lid and the other end in the mouth of the uterus.
And hold it until the steam reaches the bottom of the uterus, then have her sneeze as we said. If the placenta comes out quickly, if it remains after this treatment and does not come out, order the midwife to dip her left hand in shiraj butter or khtammi saliva.
Then insert it into the vulva and search for the placenta. If she finds it, grasp it and pull it out little by little until it comes out. If it is attached deep in the uterus, introduce the hand as described above. When the placenta is found, pull it out slowly with caution.
Lest the uterus fall when pulled hard, it should be moved gently to the sides right and left, then the amount of pulling is increased. Then it responds and gets rid of the adhesion. If the mouth of the uterus is closed, we have described the treatment by sneezing and the treatment with a pot and herbs.
If it does not come out with all that has been described, then beware of force on her in re-pulling it but rather she should tie what came out from it to the mouth of the uterus to the thigh of the woman, then inject her with the fourfold ointment, for it softens her after days.
It dissolves and comes out, except that if it has become rotten, an unpleasant odor rises from it to the stomach and head, and this harms the patient, so it is necessary to use a suitable poultice.
Therefore, and because some of the ancients experimented with a poultice of dates and dried figs, similar to the apparatus that women use for steaming when they are experiencing menstruation or after childbirth.
It is made from lead, resembling a funnel, or from copper, with the narrow end placed in the vulva and the wide end over the fire, and incense is placed on the embers, holding it until the incense burns out and then replacing it.
Chapter Seventy-Eight.
On Treating an Unpierced Rectum.
Many boys are born with unpierced rectums, sealed by a thin peritoneum, so it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this peritoneum with her finger, or else to cut it with a sharp scalpel, taking care not to touch the muscle.
Then she places a cloth soaked in syrup and oil on it, and then treats it with ointments until it heals. If she fears that it will become blocked again, put a lead tube into the hole for many days and remove it when the child wants to defecate.
It may also happen that the rectum becomes blocked due to a scar or tumor, in which case it is necessary to cut open this scar and then treat it as described above with ointment and poultices.
Chapter Eighty.
On Treating Hemorrhoids That Occur Below.
Hemorrhoids that occur below are a complication and thickening that occurs near the rectum, either outside or in the space from one of the sides, and the hemorrhoid can be one or more.
If this complication becomes inflamed and fluid, white or a thin pus, flows from it, and some of these hemorrhoids may be infused into the large intestine and small intestine, and those that are not infused can be known by what comes out with them from feces and gas when the patient uses the toilet.
Perhaps a worm may emerge from it, and it may be fistulas if it is in the open, penetrating to the bladder and the urethra. It may also penetrate to the hip joint and the coccyx. And that which is known as a fistula penetrating to the anus is also of this kind, but not the other kind.
Insert your index finger into the anus and insert a fine probe of copper or iron into the fistula if there is no constriction; but if there is a constriction, insert a fine lead probe or a hair from a horse's mane.
Until you feel the probe or hair in your finger, if you do not feel it at all and nothing emerges from the opening of feces or gas or worm as we have mentioned, then know that it is not penetrated, and hasten to treatment.
And if the fistula is penetrating to the bladder or urethra, its evidence is the exit of urine from it and its refusal to adhere to the place with medicines. But if it is penetrating to the hip joint or coccyx, its sign is the reaching of the probe there.
If it does not have a constriction to the bone and the presence of pain in its direction, and the constant exit of pus from it, and there is no remedy for it nor does it adhere to ointment, then all these penetrating fistulas are free from cure.
And their treatment is a vain effort for those who try to cure them from ignorant physicians. As for the one that is not penetrated and not chronic, it is hoped for recovery by iron as I describe it and what has been tried, which is to place the patient in your hands on his back.
And the leg is shifted upwards and the hips are tilted towards his abdomen, then a copper or lead probe is inserted if there is a constriction in the fistula until you know where it ends; if the patient feels it near the anus, then you should insert your index finger into the anus.
If you feel in your finger the probe has entered by itself uncovered and without feeling between your finger and it any scraping or flesh, then know certainly that it is penetrating. Do not tire yourself over it for there is no cure from it as we have said.
And they have said that it heals in some people rarely, and of the treatment which one hopes for benefit from, is to heat a fine iron plate according to the size of the wound as mentioned before, and insert it into the wound until it reaches near the seat, then return it twice or three times.
Until you know that it has burned all of that excess flesh which is attached like a bird's feather tube, then treat him with a poultice moistened in butter until those burned pieces come out, then treat him with the adhesive ointments if he heals.
And if not, then he does not heal without this treatment at all. But if you insert the probe and it did not penetrate to your finger in the seat, and there was a thick barrier of flesh or peritoneum between it and the probe, and you saw the wound below the skin's surface, then cut the skin from the beginning of the wound. And as you pass through the cut with the probe in the wound until you reach where the tip of the probe ended, then the probe is removed and falls, then clean those attached pieces of flesh which resemble a bird's feather tube and leave nothing of it.
Then treat him with the adhesive ointments until he heals, and if blood overpowers you and stands between you and working to cut those pieces of flesh, then the best thing you can do and the quickest benefit is cauterization by fire or with a sharp medication because cauterization by fire gathers two good states burning those excess pieces of flesh.
And cutting the blood and drying the moistness, then treat him with a poultice moistened in butter or powdered sulfur with oil until the place suppurates and those burned pieces come out in pus, then treat the wound then with adhesive ointments that are good for firming up the flesh.
These are the medicines that have constriction and drying, for if it is broken, it is healed and does not require packing. If the wound has reached the depth of the buttocks and is far from the surface of the body, insert your finger into the buttocks and search within it.
If you feel the probe and between it and you there is a curtain of peritoneum or flesh, and it was near to the penetration, there is no work to be done in it except by way of hope and expectation that you use one of three ways, either mold it as we have mentioned.
Or, you may cut it until you reach its bottom so that you can manage to insert the probe and treat from close proximity, but do not exaggerate in cutting lest you cut the muscle surrounding the buttocks, causing the patient to have involuntary bowel movements, then treat it with what we mentioned. Perhaps he will be healed as we said.
Or, you may penetrate that curtain and perforate it after you have cut it close to the buttocks as we mentioned, either with the probe or with another sharp-pointed instrument, then cleanse all of the coagulated flesh in the incision where you could reach.
Then sew together the entire wound, including the incision and the upper opening until it is closed and the wound remains open inside the buttocks, which will be easier for the patient, and perhaps the wound will close in this manner.
And if you inserted the probe into the wound and it was on one side of the buttocks towards the surface of the body, with the skin and the ring of the buttocks, then take a probe with a perforated tip like an awl in this manner:
And insert a loose thread of five threads or so into it, then insert the probe with the thread into the wound until it reaches its bottom. If it is penetrating in the edge of the buttocks from inside close by:
Then bring the thread out of that hole by inserting your finger into the buttocks and bringing out one end of the thread, and gather both ends together and tighten them, and leave it for a day or two. Every time the thread cuts in the flesh, tighten it well until that flesh between the ends of the threads falls off, then treat the wound until it heals and closes.
If the mouth of the abscess is not open, then make it open as much as you can, but do not make it too deep, lest you cut the muscle, then treat it as mentioned before until it heals.
The pointed scalpel used to open abscesses has a sharp edge on one side and a blunt edge on the other so that it does not cut what is not needed, as you see.
Chapter Eighty-One.
Concerning hemorrhoids that bleed, cutting them, and treating fissures.
Hemorrhoids come in two types: either they are inside the anus, resembling red swellings or like grapes, and some are small and others large, with blood always flowing from them.
They can be one or many, and some are outside the anus at its edges; however, these that are outside the anus are usually less moist, with a discharge of yellow water or a little blood flowing constantly, and they have the color of the body.
And the treatment for those inside the anus is to order the patient to sit and wash until the anus prolapses, so that you can see the hemorrhoids.  Quickly, you grab them with tweezers or hold them with your finger, then cut them at their base. If the tweezers do not catch because of the moisture and relaxation of the area,
then remove it with a rough cloth or a piece of cauterized bread, or pull it out with your fingers and then cut it, and after cutting, put some sharp points on top so that they perform the function of cauterization, or sear it as mentioned before in the chapter on cauterization.
Then treat it with all the other treatments until it heals. If the anus does not prolapse, inject the patient with an injection containing a small amount of laxative to wash what is inside the anus and facilitate its exit quickly when the patient cleanses himself. As for those hemorrhoids outside the anus, they are easy to manage.
It is by taking it with your finger or hanging it with a hook and cutting it, then treating it as mentioned until it heals.  And if one dislikes cutting with iron, it is necessary to employ a needle on this description. Take a loose thread and insert it into a needle.
Then you draw the  tumor upwards and insert it with the needle at its base from the other side, and wrap the ends of the thread below the needle while it is crossing over, and tighten the tumor tightly and firmly, then tie the thread and remove the needle. Do this for all the tumors and leave one of them uncauterized.
To drain excess blood from it, then place on the seat a cloth soaked in rose butter or cedar oil and place it on the seat and order the patient to be still, then leave him until it falls off. If the tumors fall off, treat them with ointments and all other treatments until they heal.
As for the treatment of anal fissures, it often occurs from fecal impaction and constipation. If it persists and no medicine benefits, it is necessary to remove it with a scalpel or your finger until it becomes moist and the outer layer that prevents it from healing is removed.
Then treat it until it heals properly. If it does not heal, repeat the excision more forcefully than before until it bleeds well and exfoliates, then treat it because it will heal.
The Eighty-Second Chapter.
In the Treatment of Ingrown Nails, both Reversed and Non-Reversed, Dry Warts, and Moles.
The nail is a rounded lump on the color of the body, resembling a nail head, which occurs in all parts of the body, especially the soles of the feet and fingers, and causes pain when walking.
It is necessary to cut around the nail, hold it with a tweezer or hook, and remove it from its root, then treat it, and if you wish, cauterize it as mentioned in its chapter. As for dry warts, one of them is a small, rough, protruding, rounded growth on the surface of the body.
It often comes to the hands of boys and its treatment is that the thorn be stretched out and cut or cauterized with silk thread or hair until it falls off, and if you wish, it can be cauterized with what has been mentioned before by fire or with a sharp drug.
And warts, both inverted and non-inverted, can be removed with the instrument that I am mentioning in the treatment of the ant.  As for the ant, it is also a small, thick outgrowth on the body's surface that goes deep inside. And if it is affected by the cold, one feels a sensation similar to an ant sting.
It is found all over the body, and most of it is found in the hands. Its treatment is that a tube is taken from an ostrich feather or a strong eagle feather and that tube is placed on the ant until it encircles the ant completely. Then you turn your hand with the tube until what surrounds the ant breaks.
And it is pushed deep into the flesh and the ant is removed from its root, and if you wish, you do this with a copper or iron tube in this image.
The top of the tube is solid and open, making it easy for the fingers to hold and control it. And if you wish, the ant can be cauterized as mentioned before in the chapter on cauterization.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
Regarding the instruments used for injection in diseases of the buttocks, diarrhea, and colic.
The syringe may be made of silver, porcelain, or brass hollowed out or hammered.  And these instruments can be made small and large according to those who use them. So, the ones used to treat young children, whose buttocks are narrow or painful, their syringes are very gentle.  Image of a large syringe.
The upper part that connects to the tube is wide, with a barrier where the tube is attached as you see. And its lower end which enters the buttocks is solid and smooth all the way to the tip. On one side there are two holes, and on the other side there is one hole.
The width of the opening should be equal to or slightly thicker than the thickness of the rod, and the tube in which the medicines are placed should be made from an animal bladder or sheepâ€™s intestines, shaped like a small plate, its diameter being about an inch.
And it is pierced with many holes as it revolves, and the distance between each hole should be the thickness of a finger, then a thick thread of doubled yarn, ten threads or so, is inserted into those holes, and the tube is gathered together like a plate. Then if medicine is placed in it, the syringe's head is pulled tight between the stones, then it is injected with it. This is a picture of the tube and the holes:
And the way to inject it is to fill the sheep's intestines or bladder with medicine while it is heated over a moderate fire, being careful that it is not too hot or too cold, then the patient lies on his back and raises his legs.
And a cushion or blanket is placed under him, then the tip of the syringe is smeared with oil or egg white or fenugreek saliva or something similar, then it is gently inserted into the rectum, and then the assistant takes the syringe in both hands and squeezes it firmly until everything in the syringe is emptied into the intestine.
Then the syringe is removed and the patient's legs are raised against the wall, if the medicine stimulates him to defecate, let him hold on as much as he can and if he sleeps all night it is more effective for constipation. If it was injected into someone with diarrhea and it hastened his bowel movement, stop the injection until he heals.
If there are hemorrhoids or painful tumors in the rectum, let the syringe be very gentle and smoother than the syringes used to inject boys, and this is a picture of a delicate syringe with its skin stretched tight:
Chapter Eighty-fourth.
In the Treatment of Wounds
I have mentioned in the division of treating things like burns, and I am mentioning here their treatment by hand and medicine to the fullest extent. So I say that wounds differ according to the thing which is operated on and according to the place where the wound occurs.
And the things in which wounds occur are many, like a stone blow or a sword cut or a knife or a spear thrust or a stick or an arrow and so on from many things.
And as for wounds according to the places in the body, such as a wound that occurs on the head or neck or chest or abdomen or liver and so on from the organs.
And I describe the treatment of some wounds to make them a measure and a law for all other wounds, and I begin with simple head wounds especially because the complex ones will be mentioned in the beginning of the third chapter of this book.
So I say that when a simple wound occurs in the head and there is no broken bone, if it is from a stone blow or the like and only the skin has been torn and the wound was large and I feared for the patient the occurrence of hot swelling, then immediately proceed to drain the cephalic on the spot. And do not delay that and bring out blood from him according to the strength of it, if nothing prevents the letting of blood then especially if the blood which comes out of the wound is easy, let the letting be from opposite the side that was wounded.
The sick person should be warned against fullness, drinks and heavy foods, for if he is prevented from his incision being performed, let him lessen his food and keep away from meat and drinks, and upon the wound if it has become hot, apply cotton soaked in rose oil alone or with a drink containing it.
And if the hot swelling is prevented, apply to the wound if it is soft with its blood and has not been changed by the air which I will describe to you shortly, as for if it has been changed by the air, apply some ointment to it.
Until it expels pus then treat it until it heals, and if the wound is large and from a sword cut or the like and its edges have not come together, join it with stitches as I describe in suturing abdominal wounds.
If the skin has exposed the bone and adhered and its hold was only in a slight attachment, cut it then treat the wound with medicines that will harden in it instead of skin, and order the sick person to eat foods that have firmness such as heads and  herbs and so on,.
If there is rot in the skin and it does not adhere to the bone, cut out all the rotten flesh and throw it away then treat it, and if in these wounds there is an artery or vein that bleeds from it and the blood does not stop with the medicines, search for the artery.
If you reach it and it does not stop, cut it off with a scalpel and tie it, and if necessity demands, if what has been mentioned did not work, cauterize it until the blood stops. And if these wounds are small and insignificant, order them easy they are easily treated by only putting this air on them when they are in their blood.
Before it changes with the air, the recipe for the air is to take from frankincense a part and from cinnamon two parts and from slaked or unslaked lime three parts, all ground together and sifted, and put it in the wound and tighten it tightly until it sticks on it well.
It is then bound with blood, and tightened above with bandages, and it is left untended until it heals, if it does not swell. For the medicine does not detach from it until it is healed, and sometimes this can be done by plaster alone if you do not have access to gum or resin.
And this can also be done with a caulk in many major wounds if it is expertly placed on them and tightened, and the wounds are fresh with blood until air changes them, but if air has changed them somewhat, especially during summer.
So, there is no meaning in treating it with what we have mentioned, by applying some mature ointments on top of it or by applying a porridge made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until it expels pus, then treating it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
But if a fracture occurs with the wound and it is slight, then draw it out with bone splints. And I mentioned the treatment of skull fractures in what follows, in the surgery of the neck, if the wound occurs in the neck, there is no difference in treatment between it and the head wound if it is simple.
But if a nerve from the neck or an artery has been cut, then if it is a nerve, there is no remedy other than to avoid treating it with something that tightens tightly like bandages and zinc oxide because they hurt the nerve and tighten it.
And nothing cold should be placed on the wound at all because the essence of the nerve is cold and it connects to the brain which is the most noble of organs, and what you treat it with from medicines should be soft like rose petals washed with fresh water several times moistened with oil or rose grease.
If you also wash with fresh water and all the minerals like this, and the moist ointments, but if the wound is large, then use sutures or close its edges with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
If the wound has a depth and there is a pus collection at its bottom, then it should be drained from the lowest point. If an artery in the wound has been severed and blood is flowing, then it should be cut, tied off, or cauterized if necessity demands it.
If the wound has cut some or all of the pharyngeal pearls and the arteries are intact, then gather the edges of the skin with sutures to the pharynx's stalk, do not touch the pharynx itself but smooth it and return it to its natural shape, then tighten it tightly and leave it for days.
Then treat it with ointments containing drying and tightening properties until it heals. If the wound has affected the bone, then open it. If there are fragments of bone inside, extract them all or as many as possible. If you cannot remove them all, leave it until the wound dries and heals, making it easier to remove them.
If the wound is moist, sprinkle it with the powders we have described. If bone dries and becomes hardened in the wound, treat it as mentioned in the chapter on chest surgery and between the shoulder blades.
If the wound was caused by a spear or knife and you see it has depth, look if air comes out when the patient breathes. If so, know that it is a mortal wound. If it doesn't have depth and is moist with blood, do not put powders in it at first nor tighten it lest blood be trapped within its depths.
It may be fatal to the patient but put an attractive ointment in it and apply it twice a day. If no ointment is available, place moistened cotton in the wound's mouth to absorb its moisture and have the patient sleep on their wound.
It will absorb what gathers there. If three days or more have passed since the wound, and the patient has no fever, shortness of breath, or any other ill symptoms and you see that their overall condition is good, know that the wound is safe. Treat it with poultices and other remedies until it heals.
If it is difficult to see the wound and the bleeding continues, know that it has become a fistulous ulcer, and treat it from its opening.  The wounded area must be drained of what collects in it. And if the wound is on the chest or back, treat it with what was previously mentioned about stitching.
If it is large or in the region of the bones, if it is small, and if it has affected the bone and fragments have been severed from it, search the wound and promptly remove those fragments. If they are clean, leave them until...
The wound is cleansed, as it makes it easier to remove them. As for the rest of wounds that occur in other organs, their treatment follows the ruling of what was previously mentioned.
The Fifth and Eighty Chapter.
On Wounds in the Abdomen and Excision and Stitching of the Intestine.
The tear that affects the abdomen can be large, small, or medium. The large one may protrude with intestines, and its re-insertion and stitching are more difficult.
The small tear can also be difficult from another perspective, requiring the intestines to be re-inserted with more difficulty. If the intestines are not promptly returned to their place within an hour, they swell and thicken, making insertion more difficult. This is why the medium tear is best, as it does not make re-inserting the intestines as difficult as these two types.
Know that suturing the abdomen has four types: the two ordinary stitches are sufficient for suturing the abdomen and all other bodily wounds, and the other two special stitches are general for all wounds except that they are more specialized for suturing the abdomen.
And I will describe them to you one by one with explanation and clarity. If the wound is small, and something from the intestine has protruded, and it is difficult to return it, this is due to one of two reasons: either because the tear is small as mentioned, or because the intestine has been inflated by cold air.
If it is so, then it is necessary to warm it by immersing a sponge or cloth moistened in lukewarm water alone or perhaps cooked with ginger and saffron and cinnamon, and rub the intestine until the bloating dissolves.
And perhaps the drink which is in it, held, is better than water alone in dissolving the bloating. And if you see that the bloating has dissolved, then swab the intestine with water cooked with cumin or caraway because it makes its entry easier and smoother.
And if it is difficult for him to return after this treatment, then make a small incision in the rupture with the instrument which you use to puncture pipes. And the first treatment if it is accomplished is better than the incision. But he is forced to make an incision only out of necessity and inability to achieve anything else. And this is the image of the instrument:
One side of it is curved and limited, the other side is unlimited, and the slender end is not sharp like a scalpel but is slightly blunt. It is an instrument that resembles a small olive as you see. And if the wound widens and the intestine enters, then it should be returned to its natural shape.
And its special place, if you can manage it, is better. But if the rupture is wide and in the lower abdomen, then he should lie on his back and make his legs higher than his head. And if it is in the upper abdomen, then make his head and chest higher than his lower parts.
And also if the rupture is on one of the sides of the abdomen, make your intention and purpose always the side that has the surgery higher than the other side. And thus it should be used in major surgeries and in medium surgeries.
And as for small surgeries, place it according to your ability. Then prepare a helper standing beside you who holds the entire rupture in his hands and gathers its edges together, then reveals them piece by piece to the one responsible for suturing.
This is the description of common single stitching, which is to take a needle or several needles according to the size of the wound, then leave from the end of the opening an amount equal to the thickness of the knuckle, and insert one needle without putting thread into its edges in the edges of the skin. With the edge of the peritoneum which is under the skin from inside until it passes through that side and I have gathered the edges of the skin and the edges of the peritoneum and they have become four folds, then tighten with a doubled thread around the needle from both sides all until the lips of the wound come together in a tight closure.
Then leave an amount equal to the thickness of the finger also and insert another needle then tighten it with the thread as you did with the first needle, so keep doing that until you need from the needles until you fill the whole wound, and let the needles be medium between thickness and thinness.
Because very thin needles quickly cut the flesh and thick ones are also difficult to enter the skin, therefore it is necessary that they be medium in thinness and thickness, and it is not necessary to insert the needle into the edge of the skin very close.
Lest the flesh be cut quickly and the wound open before it heals, and do not be distant also with the stitching lest the wound prevent from healing, then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not harm the patient when he sleeps and make for him a support from a linen opening on each side to hold the ends of the needles.
And leave them until you know that the wound has healed, and this type of stitching with needles is thus suitable in small surgeries because it may be sufficient in sewing it with one or two needles or so.
Or the description of the second common stitching is that you gather with the stitching the four edges, meaning the edges of the skin and the edges of the peritoneum in one go with a needle containing a thread twisted moderate in thinness and thickness, then if it runs out with this needle the four edges return the needle from the side where it started itself.
The thread should be placed, knotted at the top of the wound so that the suture is like the stitching used for a bag which is drawn tight and between every stitch and stitch there must be the width of a little finger and this type of stitching is known to all people.
And with this suture, a surgery was performed on a man in his belly who had been wounded with a knife and the wound was more than an inch wide and from his intestines about two inches of the middle intestine had come out and the tear was in the middle of the belly.
I laid it out after I had placed his intestines outside the wound for twenty-four hours and the wound healed in about fifteen days and I treated him until he recovered and lived for many years afterward conducting himself properly in all things and the physicians had judged that he would not recover at all.
And it is amazing that I did not treat him with ointment because I was in a place where there were no medicines at all so I put on the wound cotton wool twice a day and made sure to wash it with honey water until it healed.
And as for one type of special suture, I remember it on the basis of Galen's words which is that you begin the stitching from the skin and insert the needle from outside to inside and if the needle has reached the skin and the muscle going in a straight line along the length of the whole belly.
I left the edge of the peritoneum on the side where I inserted the needle and inserted the needle into its other edge from inside to outside in the other flap from the inspection and if you have penetrated it, then penetrate it again into this same flap from the inspection from outside to inside.
And leave the edge of the peritoneum on this side and insert the needle into its other edge from inside to outside and penetrate with your penetration in the peritoneum to the flap of the inspection which is on its side until it penetrates all of it.
Then also begin from this side with the same needle and line it with the edge of the peritoneum on the other side, and bring out the needle from the skin near it, then return it into that skin and line the edge of the peritoneum on the other side with this edge from the monitor.
And bring it out from the skin on its side, and do that once more and do it again and again until you sew all the surgery together on that example, and the sum total of the description of this sewing is to sew a fur stitch for furs.
That you sew the peritoneum once from one side with the edge of the skin and leave it once from the other side until it is empty, as for the second kind of special stitch that Galen also mentioned, this is his word exactly.
And that you sew it on the example of how some healers sew it together by gathering each part to its counterpart, naturally joining the edge of the peritoneum to its other edge and the edge of the monitor to its other edge, which is as I describe to you.
It is necessary that you insert the needle into the edge of the monitor near you from the outside and penetrate it inside alone, leaving the edges of the peritoneum, then return the needle and penetrate it from the outside to inside in both edges of the peritoneum, and return it also.
And penetrate it from inside to outside in the other edge of the monitor on the opposite side, and this type of sewing is better than the common easy sewing which is the sewing mentioned before, this is Galen's word exactly, and some have said that you can straighten the abdominal sewing with two needles. And that is to insert a single thread into them and begin by inserting the needle from where you are and penetrate it to the other side, and insert the other needle from the opposite side of it so that it penetrates from where you are according to the sewing of the straps, whether.
Know that if a rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, its stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the abdomen. As for the treatment of the wound, its ruling in treating it is like the ruling in treating all wounds, namely: when you reach the wound wet with blood before the air changes it and you have returned the intestines and outlined them and tightened them, then place upon it the crushed salt.
If the wound has been changed by the air, place upon it some of the ointments you prepare until suppuration occurs and the threads fall off and the peritoneum and the serosa unite, then treat it like the treatment of all other wounds until it heals.
If you do not have medicines, place upon it since it begins to suppurate clean cotton and change it twice a day as I have informed you until it heals.  For in most cases you do not need other treatment if the wounds are simple, but if you fear that the wound will share with the major organs pain.
It is best that you dip soft wool in moderately warm oil or rose fat and place it around the places between the ribs and armpit. If he feels pain or putrefaction in his intestines, this often occurs, then inject him with a black slightly warm astringent drink.
Especially if the putrefaction has reached the intestines and became a penetrating wound to his belly, and know that what was from the intestines thick is easier to heal, and what was from them thin is harder to heal.
As for the intestines known as the fasting, it does not accept healing from surgery that falls on it at all because of the abundance of its veins and their size and the softness of its mass and its proximity to the nature of the nerve,  but if what emerged from the wound is the intestine and reached it with a clean path, turn it back according to its return to the intestines.
If it has passed for a while and turned green or black, it is necessary to tie it with a thread above the place that blackened from it so that it does not expose bleeding because there are veins and arteries in the intestine, then cut what is below that bond.
And make the ends of the thread attached from below the surgery outside of it so that it is easy for you to pull and extract it when the intestine falls and cauterize the wound, mention the wound that occurs in the intestines, but if a tear occurs in the intestines and it is small.
It can be healed in some people because I saw a person who had been stabbed in his abdomen with a spear and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, so I sewed up the wound and it became an opening from which feces and gas came out, so I treated him as I did not hope for his healing. So I continued to treat him until he healed and the place congealed, and when I saw that the place had congealed, I feared for the patient that something bad might happen to him in his belly, so nothing bad happened to him at all and he remained in the best of conditions. Truly he eats and drinks and has intercourse and enters the bath and enjoys service, and some of the people of experience mentioned that when a wound occurs in the intestines and it is small, it should be sewn up in this way.
And it is that the large ants, their heads are taken, then the edges of the wound are gathered and an ant from them, which has its mouth open, is placed on the edges of the wound, and when it grasps it and tightens its mouth, its head is cut off, so it sticks together and does not come apart, and another ant is placed near the first.
And you continue to do this with a number of sutures equal to the size of the wound, then you return it and suture the wound because those heads remain attached in the intestine until the intestine heals and is cured, and no harm occurs to the patient at all, and the intestine can also be sutured with fine thread.
That which is drawn from the two animal parts attached to it after it enters a needle, is that the end of this thread from the two parts is taken and pulled properly, then it is tied at its end with a fine linen thread, and that thread is inserted into the needle. And in it is the thread of the two parts, with which the intestine is sutured, then returned to the abdomen, and this type of stitching with sutures and two parts is only by way of hope and desire.
But if the tear is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the delicate intestines, there is no remedy for it at all.
Chapter sixty-eight.
In the Treatment of Colds and Nasal Discharges.
Know that every wound or tumor if it has aged and progressed and become an ulcer and has not healed and continues to discharge pus, is called in general, in any organ, a  napsur, and we call it a cold.
It is, in truth, a complicated, solid white mass with no pain, and it has a cavity like the hollow of a bird's feather.
Therefore, some people called it a feather, and it may be sometimes moist and constantly discharges pus, and perhaps the moisture ceases at times. This moisture may be abundant or scanty, thick or thin.
And I have presented in the classification, when mentioning wounds, that every ulcer that does not heal and new flesh does not grow in it, is due to one of nine causes, one of which is either due to a deficiency of blood in the body, or its poor quality, or because there is solid flesh inside it and on its edges that prevents the growth of good flesh. It may be that there are many impurities and filth, or perhaps because the ulcer itself is foul and the material filling it is of poor quality, or perhaps because the medicine is not suitable for its treatment, or perhaps due to a plague that occurred in the area, or perhaps it is specific to the area.
It may be that there are many impurities and filth, or perhaps because the ulcer itself is foul and the material filling it is of poor quality, or perhaps because the medicine is not suitable for its treatment, or perhaps due to a plague that occurred in the area, or perhaps it is specific to the area. As it was presented in the city of Saragossa, where diseases are difficult to ripen and tumors are slow to heal by nature, and perhaps because it has a single bone or several bones, and all these causes and their signs and treatments with medicines have been explained in the classification.
Here, I must inform you about the treatment of abscesses and colds that occur through manual work. Know that abscesses can occur in all parts of the body, some ending in large bones, veins, or nerves.
Or to the peritoneum or intestines or bladder or rib from the ribs or vertebra from the vertebrae of the back or joint from the joints that are complex in construction like the hand and foot, and some of them lead to the vicinity of a main organ and so on.
So whatever of these abscesses is of this nature, it is one of the difficult diseases to cure and does not accept treatment, and working with it is arduous and ignorance. If it is from abscesses that have not reached these places mentioned and I have hoped and desired their cure.
And I wanted you to reach that knowledge, so take a probe from copper or iron if the abscess passes through straight, then probe it with it. If there is a complication in the abscess, then probe it with a fine lead probe because lead softens its body.
If it turns towards the complication when entering, then if the abscess has many openings that you cannot identify with the probe, inject one of its mouths, for the moisture you inject flows towards the other openings and spills.
Then, examine thoroughly in every way you can to know if there is bone or nerve, and whether the opening is far or near, or if it is one opening with many mouths.  Pay attention to all this as much as your power allows from your interrogation of the patient and his condition of pain when you touch the place.
And such are the signs and causes of tumors. If you have stood on all this with certainty, then  it is time to proceed to treatment with confidence by looking at...
The opening appears close by or in a healthy place far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or one of the places I have mentioned to you, then split the opening as described above and remove what is in it of  the hardened matter and rotten flesh and excess flesh.
And what grows in its mouth of flesh or tumor and the like, treat it until it heals. If the opening is deep and straight, it is necessary to split it deeply as much as you can, then cleanse it from all its rotten flesh.
Then use the  threaded forceps in the sharp medicines and insert them into the bottom of the opening which you can reach with iron, do this repeatedly until that sharp medicine eats up everything remaining in the bottom of the opening of rot.
Then  force it with ointments that grow healthy flesh until it heals. If it does not heal by this, do what has been described above. If the cause of the opening was bone and you are certain of that, then split it and cut it as I have told you, if nothing prevents you from doing so.
Or a nerve or main organ as we have said, if the bone was revealed to you and there was some rot and blackness in it, remove it until its rot goes away, then treat it with what grows flesh until it heals. If it does not heal and the pus continues as before.
Know that you have not reached all the removal of the corruption so reveal everything upon it again and inquire into its edge and purification with the utmost effort then force it, if it is cured, otherwise know that this corruption is in a deep place from the corruption so reveal everything upon it again.
And inquire into its edge and purification with the utmost effort if the bone was corrupted, a small bone and you could draw it forth, then draw it with the finest instruments that are suitable for this purpose.
If it is many bones, then inquire into drawing forth all of them and do not leave anything from them strive with effort if something from the ligaments obstructed you below it and it was not dangerous to cut it, then cut those ligaments and flesh if there was any and free the bones.
If it did not become easy for you to extract the bones from your time, then place upon the wound what would cover it and leave it days until it rots what is around those bones of flesh and ligaments and preserve the wound so that it does not close the opening which you made during your work.
But place upon it if you feared that, cotton soaked in powdered sulfur with oil or cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment or one of the green ointments for if it rots those ligaments and purifies the bones, it will be easy to extract them and draw them forth.
If it was a single bone large like the thigh bone or femur and such and what corrupted from it was its face only, then strip it with a sharp stripping until that blackness and corruption disappear then force the wound if what corrupted from it was a large portion and the corruption reached the marrow of the bone, there is no escape from spreading it.
And cut it all where the corruption ends then treat it until it closes, and I tell you a case of suppurating that occurred to a man in his leg to make it an example and aid for your treatment, this man was young in age.
Around his thirtieth year, a pain appeared in his leg due to movement inside the body until it reached the leg and swelled with a great tumor. There was no cause from outside, then time progressed with the error of the physicians until the tumor opened.
And from him, many materials flowed out and he was poorly treated until the leg became festering and many openings appeared in it, all of which poured pus and bodily fluids. He was treated by a group of physicians for about two years and there was no skilled one in handcraft among them.
Until they brought him to me, I saw his leg and the materials flowing from those openings in a great stream, and the man had become weak in body and his color had turned yellow. So I inserted the probe into one of those openings, and the probe reached the bone, then I widened all the openings.
And I found that some of them led to each other from all sides of the leg, so I proceeded and split on one of those openings until I exposed some of the bone, and I found it rotten, eaten away, black, putrid, and riddled with holes until the hole reached the brain. And I disclosed what was revealed to me.
And I removed the rotten bone, and I think that there is nothing in the bone other than that rot which I cut and disclosed, and that I had eradicated it. Then I made the wound close with medicinal ointments for a longer period, but it did not heal. Then I returned and exposed the bone again above the first exposure.
And I found the rot connected to the bone, so I disclosed what appeared to me of that rot as well. Then I discarded its closure, and it did not close or heal. Then I exposed it again, and I kept cutting the bone piece by piece, hoping to heal it, but it did not heal until I cut about an inch from the bone.
And I removed it with its brain, then I closed it with medicines and it healed quickly and recovered. But this repetition was necessary in his work and its splitting due to the weakness of the patient and his poor condition, and my fear for his death because he used to suffer from excessive discharge and foul waste all the time. And he recovered completely.
If a firm, fleshed-out bone has grown in its place and its condition has been consolidated within the body and its strength has receded and it has changed its state and walking did not expose it to harm whatsoever, then if a bone has broken in a place in the body .
Where it is necessary to expose it in this manner, taking a rope and tightening it at the end of the protruding bone and instructing him who extends it upwards and making another rope from wool thicker than the first rope.
Then tying it to the flesh beneath the bone and extending its end so that the flesh is drawn downwards and you expose the flesh at the place you want to expose so that the saw does not harm the flesh and place a board or plank under the bone from below tightly clamping it.
Because if you do that the saw will not prevent itself from cutting the diseased bone and it is necessary that the exposure be above the place of decay a little so that there is no decay in the cavity of the bone so that it does not appear on its surface to the touch and you will be forced to expose it once more.
If the bone is diseased and has not protruded but its parts are connected to each other and the decay is in its middle or some of it, then expose the flesh from all sides of it entirely and then place the board from below and then expose it from the first side where the decay is.
And if you have finished exposing it, expose it from the other side and let the exposure be at a distance from the decay as we have said, if the decay is in a joint you cut the decayed joint itself and expose the bone where it connects from the other side.
If the decay is in the connection of two joints there is no remedy except amputation, if the decay is in the metacarpal bone or the metatarsal bone then the matter in its treatment is very difficult but it is necessary that you scrape away the decay as much as it appears to you and remove it and cleanse it as much as you can.
By what means do you straighten it if no vein or nerve obstructs you? Know that there are many saws and chisels for cutting these bones according to the position, arrangement, thickness, thinness, size, smallness, firmness and splintering of the bone. Therefore, it is necessary to prepare a tool suitable for each kind of work.
And know that the works themselves may indicate to you the type of tool you need if you have a long experience and knowledge of the arts of this craft, because it is from the skill of the craft and seeing various diseases. For he may deduce for himself what tools to use for each disease, and I have depicted for you at the end of this chapter several tools.

The Seventy-Eighth Chapter.
In Cutting off Limbs and Spreading Bones.
Limbs may rot either from an external cause or an internal one. If you treat that corruption with medications and the treatment is ineffective, and you see the corruption spreading in the limb and nothing stops it.
Then you must cut off that limb to where the corruption has reached so that the patient is saved from death or a great misfortune, which is greater than losing the limb. A sign of someone who experiences this is that the limb turns black until you think fire burned it.
Or it rots after turning black until that corruption spreads to the next limb and takes hold of the rest of the body, so act quickly to cut it off.  And similarly if the cause of the corruption is from the sting of some insects like a sea scorpion or a snake or a viper and the like.
If the corruption or sting is in the tip of a finger, cut off the finger and do not delay for the corruption to spread to the hand. And similarly if it has taken hold of the hand, cut it off from the base of the wrist and do not delay for the corruption to spread until it takes hold of the forearm.
And similarly if it has taken hold of the arm, cut off the arm at the elbow joint itself. If the corruption persists and you see it spreading toward the shoulder, do not cut off the shoulder at all because in that case the patient will die.  And use other treatments to the best of your ability.
And do the same for the leg if the corruption takes hold in the toe, cut off the toe at one of the phalanges. If it takes hold in the foot, cut off the entire foot. If it ascends to the knee, cut off the leg at the knee joint.
If the decay has reached above the knee, there is no remedy but to leave it and entrust the patient to death. The prescription for cutting off the limb or spreading it out is to tie a bandage at the bottom of the place you want to cut, and tie another bandage above it.
And one servant extends the lower bandage and another servant extends the upper bandage, and you strip the flesh between the bandages with a broad scalpel until all the flesh is exposed, then it is cut or spread out, and it is necessary to put linen shreddings on all sides.
So that the saw does not touch the correct place, exposing the patient to additional pain and a hot swelling, if bleeding occurs during your work, quickly plug the location or place some cutting hemostatic objects on it then return to your treatment until you finish.
Then tie the wounded limb with a bandage that suits it and treat it until it heals, and I tell you an example of a case of a man in his leg this very condition that I describe to you, namely that there was blackness in his leg with a burning like fire.
And that decay was first what happened in his finger until it took the whole leg, and the man severed his own leg when he saw the decay advancing in the limb with the intensity of the pain and burning, so he cut it at the joint and healed.
And when a long time had passed, that same decay appeared in his index finger, and he came to me; I treated it with the remedies I had brought for the hand after cleaning his body, but the decay did not recede and kept advancing in the other finger.
Until the decay took hold of his hand, and he called me to cut off his hand; I refused him out of hope for me to cure that decay, and I was also afraid of his death if I cut off his hand because his strength was on the decline, so when he despaired of me, he went back to his country.
I was told about a case where a man's entire hand was cut off and he healed. This story is recounted to help with cases of this kind and to serve as a guide to be followed.
The Eight-Eighth Chapter.
On the Treatment of Abscesses and How to Inject Them with Medicine.
If a tumor occurs in some fleshy organs and the duration of the tumor extends until it gathers for a period, then it bursts or ruptures, expelling all that was contained within it from the matter, leaving the site empty like a vessel.
And the skin on it, like a piece of cloth, has become loosened and has not been so severely corrupted that it affects bone or nerve or tendon. And from here it deserves to be called an abscess, and it is not called a fistula unless its duration extends until corruption affects something of these organs.
Then it is called a fistula or a carbuncle, and its treatment is to cut all of that skin completely as it revolves, especially if it has loosened and become like a piece of cloth, and you are certain that it does not adhere to the site due to its corruption.
If you fear that the skin will adhere, and it has not reached that level of corruption, and there is a thickness of flesh in the skin, then its treatment is by injection, which is to look at the abscess. If it is large and the pus that flows from it is foul-smelling, inject it with Egyptian medicine.
Which is honey, oil, and wax, and ginger in equal parts are gathered in a vessel and cooked on fire until the medicine thickens and comes to the thickness of honey. Then you take from it what you need and soften it with water and honey, and inject it into the abscess, tighten its opening, and leave the medicine inside for two hours.
Then you extract it at noon. Do this for several days until the abscess is cleansed and the stench disappears. And he may be injected with ash water if this medicine is not available to you, which is to take the ash of sandalwood or oak wood and put water on it.
Then wash it and inject it until you are certain that the cavity has been washed out. If there is no possibility of using Egyptian medicine or ash water in the patient, inject him with water mixed with honey and a little powdered ginger.
Or inject him with honey and syrup mixed together, because honey cleanses and washes, and the syrup adheres to the cavity, especially if the syrup contains a good amount of dryness and congealed consistency. When you have done this several times and are certain that the cavity has been rid of its corruption, then inject it with something that promotes the growth of flesh in it.
Such as taking palm ointment and dissolving it in rose oil and astringent syrup, or injecting him with some of the other medicines and ointments whose properties we have established in the article on ointments. If the opening of the cavity is narrow and does not allow for the syringe to be inserted.
Then widen it slightly with iron or place a piece of gauze soaked in Egyptian ointment or licorice ointment inside until it widens. Likewise, if the opening is also wide, gather its lips together with stitches and leave only as much as allows the syringe to enter without excess.
And likewise, if the opening from which the pus flows is elevated upwards, cut it in its lowest place so that the pus flows downwards because if the pus stagnates in the depths of the cavity, it prevents flesh from growing there.
So if you cannot cut the cavity downwards as you desire, then form the member in a way that allows the pus to flow out easily, according to what seems appropriate to you, and make sure that nothing of the pus is retained at all.
As for the solid medicines that are placed on the cavity from the outside and how to place them, take one of the solid ointments suitable for what you desire and spread it on a linen cloth, making sure the cloth is large enough to cover the entire cavity. Then you cut with the knife opposite the opening of the abscess, a hole a little wider than the opening, then you spread a soft ointment on a piece of linen cloth the size of the hole and place it over it, placing it at a distance from the opening so that pus can easily exit from it. Do not remove the large cloth until later.
For several days, but the one on the opening of the abscess is removed at all times so that what has accumulated there of pus may exit and to know what flows from it, whether it is much or little, ripe or unripe.
And with this also, inspect the site of the abscess itself, whether its owner feels pain in it or not, and whether there is a swelling or not. If you persist in treating it like this and see that the matter that exits is slight on the opening of the abscess...
... then know that the abscess has scabbed over or is close to scabbing over, so at that time, cut it open tomorrow or on the third day. And when you have opened the wound, replace the cloth with another and renew the ointment. If after a long period pus flows out thin from the abscess, do not despair of its healing.
For it is close to healing because some people are slow in the growth of flesh in their wounds and others are the opposite. If after many days pus flows out from the abscess that is unripe, know that the abscess has not healed, and if the healing of the abscess is delayed.
And if the matter is prolonged, increase in drying the medications and let them be medications that are in their consistency moist and in their strength dry, like the palm ointment if it has been increased with an excess of qalqatar. And among the most effective things to treat it is to take the palm ointment.
And it is treated with rose butter and sprinkled on it the ancient syrup moderate in its consistency, then plastered with it and used. And he may do this if the palm ointment is not available for him. Honey if it has been cooked until it thickens and used or take from saffron, patience, and licorice and crush them all together and sprinkle them on honey while it is on the fire. Then it is covered with a cloth and tightened over the wound, or it is coated with honey which has been cooked until it thickens, and the medicines are placed on it and the cloth is put on top and tightened.
And in a similar manner, long saffron, the root of asphodel, ground cypress seeds, and coriander, individually or together, are crushed, sieved, and sprinkled on the honey described above.  If the wound persists for a long time and does not heal with this treatment, know that there is corruption within it.
And it has been effective in bones or in all solid nerves or ligaments, its treatment is as previously described.
Chapter Eighty-Nine.
In the Treatment of Ingrown Nails, Malformed Toenails, Excision of Extra Finger and Separation of Fused Fingers.
An ingrown toenail is a large amount of flesh that grows under the toenail of the big toe or foot, and possibly in other toes. If it persists and its treatment is neglected, there will be swelling and hot pus.
Or it festers and becomes putrid until it eats the root of the nail, possibly damaging the entire nail, and perhaps the corruption reaches the bone until it has a foul odor and the tip of the finger becomes wide and its color turns black. If you treat it with what was mentioned in the previous section and your treatment is ineffective.
Then it is necessary to cut with a knife all the excess flesh that grows from the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards. For cauterization in this case is very beneficial. But if the bone is sound and the nail is also sound.
And if the corner of the nail has driven the flesh inwards and made it ulcerate and suffer, then it is necessary to place a thin piece of cloth under the corner of the nail that is driving the flesh in and raise it upwards, and cut that flesh gently.
And you place on what remains of the flesh from the burning drugs, until it all goes away, then treat it with ointments until it heals. But if the corruption has affected the bone, it is necessary to cut that bone and remove it, because it will not heal as long as there is a rotten bone at all.
If you see the corruption and putrefaction spreading in the finger, cut it off at one of the joints as mentioned before, then treat it until it heals. If the nail was struck or injured and there was severe pain, it is necessary to cauterize the ailment first.
Then you split the nail with a sharp scalpel, a slanted cut from top to bottom, and be careful not to reach with the cut to the flesh under the nail, because by doing that, you will cause severe pain for the patient and it will be the cause of extra flesh growing in the place. Then treat the place with something that soothes the pain.
As for the extra finger that is born in some people's hands, it may be all flesh and perhaps it has bone in some of it, and perhaps it has a nail, and its growth may be at the root of a joint of one of the fingers.
Or its growth may be in some of the joints of the finger, and what grows in some of the joints of the finger does not move, and what grows at the joint of the finger may move, so if it is only fleshy, it is easy to cut it off by cutting it at its root with a wide scalpel.
But as for the one whose growth is at the root of the joint, its treatment is difficult, so you avoid cutting it. But as for the one that grows in the finger at one of the joints, it is necessary to first cut its flesh with a round cut to the bone, then spread the bone with one of those saws suitable for that.
Then treat it until it heals. But as for the adhesion that occurs to some fingers with each other, it often occurs and is what a person is born with, and it may be when closing a wound or burn and so on, so it is necessary to split that adhesion.
Until the fingers return to their natural shape, then place between them a spatula or incision soaked in rose butter so that it does not quickly adhere and separate them, or put between them a thin sheet of lead until the place heals as it should.
And also if the adhesion of some fingers to the palm appears, then split that adhesion according to what appears suitable and repairs the shape of the limb.
Chapter Ninety.
On Cutting Off Joints.
Joints are twisted veins, thick and filled with black phlegm, which occur in most parts of the body, and they appear more frequently in the legs, especially in those who work heavily like carriers, woodcutters, and laborers. Therefore, it is necessary first to use a strong poultice of black soap on the affected area.
Then, it is cut with a sharp instrument, and the treatment of these joints by iron comes in two ways: one is to make an incision and remove the black blood, and the other is to cauterize the vein and remove it entirely. As for the incision method, the leg is first bathed in hot water.
Until the thick, dark blood is dissolved, then the patient's leg is tightly bandaged from above the groin to below the knee with a cloth, and then the vein is cut in one place, or two places, or three places with a wide incision.
Then, black blood is squeezed from the bottom of the leg up to the top and from the top down until the amount you deem sufficient or that which the patient can withstand is removed. Then, it is tied and he is instructed to avoid foods that produce black phlegm, and this process of cupping and letting out blood is repeated.
When the veins are full and this harms the patient, as for cauterization, it is done in this way: the patient's leg is shaved if it has a lot of hair, then he is put in the bath, and his leg is bathed in hot water until it becomes red and the vein becomes visible or there is a strong feeling of heat.
If a bath is not available to warm the limb, then the skin is cut along the groin, either at the back of the knee or below it at the heel, and the skin is opened with forceps and the sweat gland is scraped from every side until it is felt.
When it appears, you will see it red and swollen. When it is freed from the skin, you will also see it like a tendon. Then, a probe is inserted under it until it rises and exits the skin, whereupon a blunt smooth forceps is used to tie it. Then another incision is made near that incision, about three finger-widths wide.
Then the skin is scraped from over the sweat gland until it appears, and then it is raised with a probe as before and tied with another forceps as before. Then another incision or several incisions are made if needed.
Then the gland is pulled and cut at the bottom incision at the heel, and it is drawn and scraped until it exits the second incision. Then it is pulled to the incision above it, and this is repeated until it is pulled from the third incision, the highest of all the incisions. When all of it has emerged, it is cut.
If it does not come out when pulled and scraped, insert a needle with a strong doubled thread and tie it, then pull it and insert a probe under it and feel with your hand in all directions until it emerges. Pay attention to ensure it does not break; if it breaks, it will be very difficult to pull.
And a probe is inserted into the wound and, when it has all been removed, a poultice soaked in syrup and rose oil or ointment is placed on the surgical site and treated until it heals. If the sweat gland is constricted with ridges and twists in various directions.
And if it is not straight as we have said, it is necessary to make an incision along each ridge and twist. Then tie it with forceps until you scrape it all together. Be careful when making the incisions that you do not cut or injure the sweat gland, because it will be difficult to remove then.
